Zhang Shizhao Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 96

Zhang Shizhao, a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, flew to Shanghai on a China National Aviation Corporation Shanghai-Ping plane yesterday afternoon. At 6:10 PM, he landed at Hongqiao Airport. After getting off the plane, Zhang went straight back to his residence on Yuyuan Road to rest. It is reported that Zhang came here to mourn Duan Qirui and plans to stay in Shanghai for a while to assist in Duan's funeral.

Overseas Polish Officials and Civilians Celebrate Independence Day 97

Yesterday was the 18th anniversary of Polish independence. The Polish Embassy in China and the Consulate General in Shanghai, as well as Polish companies and firms, were all closed and flags were hung to celebrate. However, there was no official reception. Only the Polish Minister to China, Wei Dentao, led overseas Chinese in prayer and joint celebration by officials and civilians.

Poland was an independent country until the end of the 18th century. Due to internal wars and external troubles, the country was divided and became a vassal of other countries. At the beginning of the European War, Poland was also caught in the vortex. In 1915, the entire territory was occupied by the Austrian-German army. On November 9, 1918, it declared independence. Two days later, General Pi Sutzuki was released from Magdeborg Prison and returned to Poland, taking full control of the country and convening the National Assembly. On June 28, 1919, its independence was recognized by the Treaty of Versailles. In 1929, China and Poland signed a treaty of friendship. Since then, the diplomatic relations between the two countries have become increasingly close, especially in cultural cooperation.

Italian National Day Receptions Guests to Receive Congratulations Italian Ambassador and Others Host Wu Mayor and Others Go to Congratulate 98

Yesterday was Italian National Day. Italian expatriates in Shanghai took a holiday and hung flags to celebrate. The Italian Ambassador to China, Luo Yaguno, and the Consul General in Shanghai, Ni Long, hosted Chinese and foreign guests at the Building at 285 Zhao Bishop Road in the French Concession from 11:30 AM to 12:30 PM to receive congratulations. Wu Tiecheng, the Mayor of Shanghai, Yang Hu, the Commander of the Songhu Garrison, Zhou Jue, the Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as British Consul General Brennan, French Consul General Bobais, American Consul General Gass, Japanese Consul General Wakasugi, and Belgian Consul General Tan Erfu, etc., all went to congratulate them. Ambassador Luo and Consul General Ni and others entertained them warmly and everyone had a good time.

Li Sihao Talks About His Meeting with President Jiang Reported and Asked for Instructions on Negotiations in Principle Met with Foreign Minister Zhang and Others in More Concrete Talks - Scheduled to Leave Shanghai and Fly Back to Ping on the 16th - 99

Li Sihao, Chairman of the Economic Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, went to Hangzhou from Shanghai on the 6th and flew to Luoyang to meet with President Jiang. He returned south to Beijing on the 8th and visited Director-General Zhang and Director-General Wu and other authorities. He left Beijing by car at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday and returned to Shanghai. He arrived in port at 10:50 PM last night. Yesterday morning at 9:00, he went to the Duan residence on Avenue Joffre to assist in the funeral arrangements. A reporter from the New Sound Society paid a special visit. According to his account, he left Shanghai for Hangzhou on the 6th, originally intending to return to his ancestral home in Cixi to handle the funeral of his uncle. However, he received a telegram from President Jiang summoning him urgently, so he flew to see him to report and ask for instructions on everything. However, the discussion was only on general principles. President Jiang highly praised the painstaking efforts of Commissioner Song (Zheyuan). Regarding economic cooperation, he said that under the principles of "not losing sovereignty" and "not containing aggression", it could be carried out at an appropriate time, and he frequently inquired about the passing of Mr. Duan and expressed his condolences. He stayed in Luoyang for one day and one night and returned south to Beijing on the 8th. He successively visited Secretary-General Weng, Foreign Minister Zhang, Director-General Wu, Director-General Zhang Tie, and others. He originally intended to return to Shanghai the night before last, but he postponed it to wait for a meeting with Director-General Zhang Tie. After Zhang flew from Shanghai to Beijing yesterday to meet with him, he returned to Shanghai last night. He said that he had met with various responsible officials in Beijing and had relatively concrete discussions on economic cooperation in North China. He had discussed the methods, but the content was not convenient to disclose. He is now scheduled to take a plane north to return to Ping on the 16th. However, because he has been away from Ping for a long time and official duties are urgently awaiting handling, he may need to leave one or two days earlier. His family originally planned to go as well, but his wife is currently ill and it has been postponed. He will return south again at the beginning of next month to assist in Mr. Duan's opening of the memorial service and moving the spirit.

Wang Yitang Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning, Talks Freely About the North China Problem, Says Danger Can Occur at Any Time, Advocates National Unity on Foreign Policy, Came Specifically to Offer Condolences to Duan, Will Return North Immediately 100

Wang Yitang, a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council, arrived in Shanghai at 7:40 AM yesterday morning, having traveled south on the Tianjin-Shanghai through train on the evening of the 9th to offer condolences for the death of Duan Qirui. After disembarking at the North Station, he first went to the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road to rest. He then went to the Duan residence on Avenue Joffre around 10:30 AM to offer condolences. Given the current situation in North China, Wang is indeed a figure worthy of close attention. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency made a special visit to the Duan residence and was granted an audience, during which they spoke freely about everything. The following is a record of their conversation:

Here Solely to Offer Condolences to Duan

Wang began by saying, "It has been a year and a half since I last came to Shanghai. As I am getting old, I have been整理 my old works and have been frequently ill. If it were not for Mr. Duan's funeral, I would not have wanted to come to Shanghai. I will stay briefly and then return north. I will come again when the date for Mr. Duan's funeral is set."

The Situation in North China

Regarding the situation in North China, "Before I resigned from the Standing Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council, I had a relatively detailed understanding. Since resigning from the Standing Committee this spring, I only hold the title of member and do not ask about much, so I do not know much. However, the danger in North China has always been imminent. At present, the situation in Suiyuan is relatively tense, while there is nothing happening in Chahar. It is estimated that the rebellious bandits who invaded Suiyuan include the troops of Li Shouxin, Wang Ying, and others. Now, the focus of the northern situation has almost shifted to Suiyuan. Since negotiations are currently underway at the central level, it is not appropriate for unexpected events to occur."

Difficult to Predict

At this point, the reporter asked about his observation of the future of the situation. He replied, "This is difficult to predict. It depends on how the future changes, the results of the central negotiations, and the evolution of the local situation. Everything is interconnected."

Foreign Policy Stance

Wang continued, "Regarding North China's foreign policy, I had negotiations before Huang Yingbai went north three years ago. I also visited Chairman Chiang in Lushan two years ago, and my trip to Japan last year was not without its purpose. Since resigning from the Standing Committee, I have had little contact with the Japanese side. My foreign policy opinion is that, regardless of whether it is tough or flexible, friendly or resistant, successful or unsuccessful, the only requirement is that 'the entire country must be united; if the entire [country] is not united, it is a weakness.' Now, all parties in our country have realized this. For example, Mr. Duan's resolute move south earlier was to demonstrate the spirit of united action. I do not know anything about the details of the recent Sino-Japanese diplomatic negotiations, so it is difficult for me to express my opinion."

Economic Cooperation

As for Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, "I discussed it with Foreign Minister Zhang this spring when I met him in Qingdao. I believe that if it is based on the principle of 'equality and mutual benefit,' not only Japan but any country can talk about cooperation. However, if it contains the meaning of aggression, then it should be discussed separately."

Huie Bank Issue

Finally, the reporter asked about the revival of the Zhonghua Huie Bank. Wang said, "I am one of the shareholders of the bank. Since being elected as the general manager in the 23rd year [of the Republic], I have never had any contact. According to the bank's creditor-debtor relationship, the credits include 15 million owed by the government, and the debts are 4 million in deposits and over 800,000 in banknotes. The bank's organization has an equal number of Chinese and Japanese directors and supervisors. In addition to myself as the general manager, the deputy general manager is Japanese. The Chinese directors are Li Sihao, Cao Rulin, and Zeng Yunpei, and the supervisors are Duan Honggang and Zeng Rongfu. At present, both Chinese and Japanese shareholders are unwilling to resume [operations], so there is no need to negotiate. In the future, if both parties agree and there is an opportunity, it may be possible to proceed."

U.S. Mail Ship Last One Enters Port Today, No Ships Arrive from Any Route Thereafter, Import of Goods Blocked, Huge Damage 101

The U.S. seamen's strike has lasted for 13 days, and there is no sign of the unrest subsiding. U.S. mail ships sailing to the Far East have been implicated in the strike. The Pacific Company's Portland and San Francisco routes have no ships coming. Of the four major mail ship routes under the jurisdiction of the Doolan Company (New York, San Francisco, Seattle, and World routes), only the President McKinley is the last ship on its westward mail route to Shanghai today. From then on, no ships will arrive. If the unrest is not resolved soon, U.S. ships traveling west in the Pacific will temporarily disappear from the Far East. U.S. goods handled by major foreign firms in this port, whether loaded or not, cannot be transported to Shanghai, and the import of U.S. goods will also be blocked from today onwards. The magnitude of the loss is difficult to estimate for the time being. As for the export goods from Shanghai to the U.S., Doolan and others are trying to prevent them from being blocked, but loading and unloading will be difficult once they enter the U.S.

Japanese Merchant Ship Sailor Takase Shot to Death Last Night, Incident Occurred in the Eastern District of the Concession, Victim Died Instantly, Assailant Fled, Municipal Government Orders Cooperation in Arresting the Murderer 103

At 8:30 PM last night, a Japanese man was shot to death at the entrance of Taoyuan Lane on Baker Road in the Public Concession. The deceased was named Yasuharu Takase, 46 years old, a sailor on the Japanese Mail Steamship Company's Kasagi Maru. Takase was walking at the entrance of Taoyuan Lane with a Japanese woman when he was suddenly shot once by an unknown person. The bullet hit his left chest. The assailant fled without a trace. The Japanese woman who was with him shouted for help and rushed the injured man by car to the Fumin Hospital on North Sichuan Road for treatment. However, because the injury was to a vital part, he died en route before reaching the hospital. Upon receiving the report, the Huishan Police Station immediately dispatched a large number of detectives to the scene to search, together with police officers sent by the Japanese Consulate. It was reported that the Concession police found a .32 caliber Browning pistol and one shell casing at the scene. The Japanese Naval Landing Force also sent a team to guard the area, cutting off pedestrian traffic. They photographed and drew diagrams of the scene. Traffic gradually resumed at 11:15 PM. After receiving the report, the Municipal Government immediately instructed the Public Security Bureau to cooperate with the Concession police to arrest the murderer. The deceased left behind a wife and two children, all in Kobe. The Japanese woman who was with him last night was a waitress at a bar named Abe, 31 years old.

It is also understood that Lu Dingnan, a fruit vendor who has been setting up a stall in the lane, was summoned by the police to inquire about the circumstances of the incident. At present, they are closely pursuing leads to arrest the murderer.

Duan Family Fetes Staff of Funeral Committee Last Night 104

The Duan Yuzhi Funeral Committee has decided to hold the memorial service on the 6th of next month and to move north to Beiping on the 7th, which is very soon, and is actively preparing everything. The Duan family specially hosted a banquet at their residence at 8 PM last night for all the staff of the funeral committee to show their appreciation and gratitude.

Labor Strike at Japanese Textile Mills Still Serious, Over a Thousand Workers' Petition Blocked, Social Affairs Bureau Sends Representatives to Meet with Funatsu to Discuss, Mills Hold Foremen's Meeting to Plan Resumption of Work, City General Labor Union Holds Emergency Meeting to Discuss Assistance 105

Following the joint strike by workers at the Japanese-owned Shanghai Tongxing, Donghua, Dakang, and other mills in the Pudong district of Shanghai, the situation has continued to escalate because the mill owners have not sincerely accepted the five demands of the workers. Yesterday morning at 6:00 AM, over a thousand male and female workers from the mills gathered on Huangxing Road and marched in a procession to the Municipal Government to petition, carrying huge banners with the words "Shanghai Textile Mill Workers' Petition Group Going to the Municipal Government to Petition." Suddenly, several Public Concession Grant Road police cars and Japanese Marines trucks gathered to monitor them. Subsequently, the Yinxianggang Police Station, seeing the large number of people and fearing an accident, sent the entire police force to persuade them to stop. Thirteen representatives from the Shanghai Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth Mills, Tongxing, Dakang, Donghua, and other mills (names withheld at their request) were selected by the workers on the spot and taken to the station for questioning. After receiving the report, Liang Fuchu, Director of the North Station Branch Bureau, also rushed to suppress the situation with a large number of police officers. Fortunately, the Public Security Bureau handled the situation appropriately, so no disturbances occurred.

Social Affairs Bureau Representative Visits Funatsu

After receiving the report from the Public Security Bureau, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau immediately sent Zhu Guilin, a mediator from the Third Section, to the Yinxianggang Police Station. He hired cars to escort the thirteen worker representatives from the mills to the Social Affairs Bureau. Wang Xianqing, Director of the Mediation Section of the Third Section, inquired about the truth of the strike and the five demands. He then advised the representatives to inform all workers to wait quietly for a resolution to avoid the expansion of the labor unrest. At 4:30 PM in the afternoon, the Social Affairs Bureau again sent Director Wang, accompanied by mediator Zhu Guilin, to the fourth floor of the Yokohama Specie Bank on the Bund to meet with Funatsu Tatsuiichiro, Chairman of the Japanese Textile Association in China, to inquire about the situation of the various strikes and the attitude of the mills towards this labor unrest. Funatsu replied that the striking mills had already agreed to increase wages by 5%, and the workers' sudden strike was hindering the mills' operations. They ended the conversation at 5:40 PM.

Dakang Still Suspended, Donghua Resumes Work

Since the night shift at the Tengyue Road Dakang Textile Mill joined the strike on the evening of the 10th, yesterday morning at 5:45 AM, the mill sounded the steam whistle and sent several large trucks to the workshops to load Japanese workers onto the trucks. They were escorted by Japanese Marines to work in the mill. They were released at 12:00 PM noon. Because two-thirds of the workers did not stay in the workshops, the machines could not be fully started, so they could not work. The night shift was still suspended. In addition, the Donghua Textile Mill on Huade Road agreed to increase wages and accepted the workers' demands. Yesterday morning, they resumed normal day and night work.

Japanese Textile Mills Hold Managers' Meeting

Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China held a meeting of managers of various Japanese textile mills in Shanghai at the Japanese Club at 295 Peng Road. Funatsu, Chairman of the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China, Kuroda from Shanghai, Okajima from Tongyu, Ishida from Donghua, Horiuchi from Dakang, Katsuda from Naigaiwata, Suzuki from Kongda, Tomonaga from Nikka Yuenaga, Hishida from Yufeng, Nishikawa from Toyota, and others from Shihe, totaling more than ten people, attended. Funatsu presided over the meeting until it adjourned at 4:10 PM in the afternoon. The Dagong News Agency reporter met with Funatsu at the Japanese Club yesterday and asked about the content of the meeting. According to his reply, the managers' meeting was to report on the recent situation of the Shanghai and other textile mills that were on strike. They exchanged consistent opinions and did not make any specific decisions. The mill owners had agreed to increase wages by 5% to meet the workers' demands and hoped that the workers would resume work soon. Otherwise, the losses due to the strike may lead to a long-term shutdown. For many years, the textile industry has been in a slump, and most mills have been losing money. There have been frequent reports of Chinese textile mills shutting down or reducing work, but our country's textile mills are more financially secure, so even though they are losing money first, they are still struggling to maintain operations. Just as the situation in the textile industry showed a slight turnaround in the last month or two, the workers demanded wage increases, which is contrary to common sense and hinders the development of industry.

Mills Convene Foremen's Meeting to Discuss

Yesterday afternoon at 1:15 PM, the Japanese-owned Shanghai First, Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth, and Sixth Mills and the Tongxing Second Mill convened a meeting of foremen from various departments, which adjourned at 4:30 PM in the afternoon. According to a foreman who spoke to the Dagong News Agency reporter, the mill owners convened the foremen today (yesterday) to discuss issues such as resuming work. It was decided that the head foremen would notify the workers to resume work and prepare to start the night shift at 6:00 PM this afternoon. After the foremen of the various departments notified the workers, they held a meeting of representatives from the various mills at a certain location. As a result, it was determined that the mills must formally accept the five demands before work could resume.

Municipal Government Hopes for an Early Resolution

The Dagong News Agency reporter went to the Municipal Government to meet with Secretary-General Yu Hongjun yesterday afternoon around 3:00 PM to inquire about how the authorities should handle the labor unrest at the Japanese textile mills. Because Secretary-General Yu was attending a meeting, Secretary Guo Shihui met with him instead. Secretary Guo replied that the Social Affairs Bureau was mediating the labor unrest and the Municipal Government hoped that both parties would meet each other frankly. Under the principle of rationality, they hoped that the labor unrest at the Japanese textile mills would be resolved soon.

City General Labor Union Discusses Assistance

The City General Labor Union believed that the workers at the Japanese textile mills could not bear the oppression of the capitalists. They had put forward five demands, which were not accepted, leading to a labor unrest. So far, it has not been resolved, and the labor unrest is tending to expand. In addition to sending people to investigate the truth, the union convened an emergency meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM to discuss assistance measures. Committee members Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Xuexiang, Li Mengnan, Ye Xianggao, Long Peiyun, Shao Xubai, and others attended. After discussion, they decided to (1) send people to express their condolences, (2) petition the party and government agencies to quickly devise effective measures, and (3) plan effective assistance measures and, if necessary, convene all labor unions in the city to discuss the measures.

Men and Women Missing, Female Worker Injured

When male and female workers from the Japanese-owned Shanghai and other textile mills went to work and left work at the Dakang Textile Mill at 6:00 PM the night before, thousands of people mixed together, causing chaos. A female worker from the Shanghai Second Mill's cotton waste department, living in Laowenyuanfang, was injured in the ear by a wooden stick. In addition, Shi Weixiang, a male worker from the Tongxing B class North Group department and from Yancheng, suddenly went missing. Representatives sent by the workers from the various mills inquired at the Yulin Road and Grant Road police stations and the Dakang Textile Mill, but there was no trace of him.

Textile Mill Area Under Heavy Guard

Since the labor unrest broke out at the Japanese-owned Shanghai and other nine textile mills in the Pudong district, the situation has become increasingly serious. The area from Gongda Second Textile Mill on Yangshupu Road to Dinghai Road on Yangshupu Road, where the textile mills are located, has entered a stage of heavy guard. In addition to the police stations sending Chinese and foreign detectives to be stationed on duty in rotation, yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, nine military vehicles from the Japanese 9th, 10th, 11th, 12th, 13th, 14th, 17th, 18th, and 22nd Divisions, carrying more than 100 soldiers, were distributed along the way. At 11:30 AM, the Japanese Marines' tank and motorcycle team patrolled back and forth on Yangshupu Road, and the security was quite strict.

Strike at Japanese-Owned Meihua Dyeing Factory

The Meihua Printing and Dyeing Factory, opened by a Japanese named Fukuzo on Hejian Road in Pudong, which employs more than 120 male and female workers, also went on strike last night and put forward five demands: (1) a general wage increase of 5 cents per person (calculated daily), (2) no reduction in the number of workers, (3) if the factory's business is slack and wages are not available, meal subsidies should be provided, (4) eating should not interrupt the machines, and the bonus should be increased every month, and (5) the night shift should be counted as one shift at 12:00 AM, and two shifts after 72 hours. Currently, Takahashi, an engineer from the factory, is representing the factory and has agreed to increase wages by 2 cents. Because the conditions are not close to agreement, the unrest is still ongoing.

Wage Increase Issue Resolved at Shenxin First and Eighth Mills 106

A general increase of 5% on the salaries at the Shenxin First and Eighth Textile Mills in Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai, the wages of all the workers was decided upon because of the recent strong sales of yarn and the improvement in business. Therefore, the Tenth District Cotton Textile Industry Union petitioned the party and government agencies for a solution. After receiving the petition, the Social Affairs Bureau summoned both labor and management to the bureau for mediation the day before. Because the opinions of the two sides were still difficult to reconcile, mediation was continued again at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Weng Shanhe and Wen Renliang from the labor side, Hua Jianren and Ling Baisheng from the factory side, and Lu Yinchu, a representative from the Municipal Party Headquarters, attended. Zhu Jintao from the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau presided over the meeting. After mediation, two resolutions were decided as follows: (1) The wages of day laborers and pieceworkers at the Shenxin First and Eighth Mills who had their wages reduced since September 1 last year will be increased by 5% across the board (the percentage is calculated based on the wages of September 1 last year). (2) If the workload of workers in various departments of the factory has increased since September 1 last year, even if their wages have not been reduced, their existing wages should also be increased by 5% across the board. Both parties expressed satisfaction with the resolution and announced the resolution.

All Circles Donate Funds for Aircraft for Birthday Congratulations 107

Various schools and groups are enthusiastically promoting the donation of aircraft for birthday congratulations in this city. One million yuan has been confirmed for donation. The Aircraft Purchase Commemoration Committee has transferred more than 700,000 yuan to the Chiang Kai-shek Birthday Aircraft Donation Commemoration Association. The remaining funds will be vigorously promoted by the association to various groups and individuals who have pledged to donate but have not yet submitted or collected donations. Yuehan Railway's 18 Stations Handle Passenger Interline Traffic 108

After the entire Yuehan Railway is completed and opened to traffic in early October, it is actively preparing for national state-owned railway passenger and freight interline traffic. It was previously reported to the Ministry of Railways that the stations on the Hunan-Hubei section of the railway had already joined the freight interline traffic. The price list for interline traffic from Zhuzhou to Sanshui has been compiled and can be implemented on a regular basis. As for passenger interline traffic, in addition to the original Liling and Anyuan stations, which belong to the Zhuping branch line, which will be transferred to the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway for management, the four stations of Wuchang East Station, Puchi, Yueyang, and Changsha East Station have already joined passenger interline traffic and will continue to operate. In addition, the 18 stations of Wuchang Main Station, Yijiawan, Zhuzhou, Hengshan, Hengyang Chenxian, Pingshi, Lechang, Qujiang, Yingde, Lianjiangkou, Yuanze, Yinzhan'ao, Xinjie, Guangzhou South Station, Foshan, Southwest, and Sanshui will be added to domestic passenger interline traffic to handle passenger luggage, parcels, and passenger car interline traffic. The standard one-way passenger ticket price list and the round-trip price list for sightseeing have been drafted and approved by the Ministry of Railways to be implemented on the 1st of this month. Three Financial Giants: Yoshida Returned to Japan Yesterday Morning; Subtly Promoting Trade with China; Easing Internal Conflicts Within Japan 111

Huadong News Agency reports that Yoshida of the Mitsubishi Zaibatsu of Japan (i.e., the manager of the Shanghai branch of Mitsubishi Bank and chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce) took a Japanese ship back to Japan at 9 a.m. yesterday. The ostensible mission is to attend Mitsubishi Bank's affairs. However, after days of investigation and visits by Huadong News Agency reporters, it is learned that he is subtly promoting the import of Japanese goods into China. Since last winter, the smuggling of Japanese goods has indeed made huge profits in the north, undermining China's economic front and ravaging China's financial system. However, on the other hand, it has given the Chinese people extreme stimulation, with mutual warnings not to buy Japanese goods, which has seriously affected legitimate merchants. Therefore, conflicts of interest have arisen between the Mitsubishi and Mitsui factions and those who specialize in smuggling in the north. At present, legitimate Japanese financial circles, in the midst of Sino-Japanese diplomatic discussions, absolutely advocate cautious handling and do not advocate resuming war. Many directors of the Japan-China Trade Association of the Mitsubishi system are also strongly advocating following Britain's lead and implementing credit loans in order to restrain China in a gentle way. Only in this way can so-called credit investment develop its power and functions in the north, and not be monopolized by the Xingzhong Company faction. For nearly two years, in addition to expanding its economic power along the Yangtze River, the Mitsubishi Zaibatsu has been unable to gain a foothold in the north. This time, Yoshida's return to Japan is to present various opinions obtained in Shanghai to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so that the specific wishes of the Japanese financial community can be stated during diplomatic negotiations. On the one hand, he will reconcile the financial groups of the Japanese Kwantung Army in Tianjin and make their opinions consistent.

Balancing Tax Continues to Rise Yesterday 112

Xinxin News Agency reports that the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee, jointly established by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, is paying attention to the balancing tax rate for preventing silver exports at a time when international silver prices are rising. The balancing tax rate was raised to 15-16% the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, due to the continued rise in silver prices, in order to prevent speculators from taking the opportunity to export silver, the balancing tax rate was further raised to 21.25%, breaking the highest record since the beginning of autumn. As for the exchange rates for telegraphic transfers to the UK, USA, France, Germany, Japan, etc., they were the same as the day before yesterday, with no changes. This is due to the effect of the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in stabilizing foreign exchange.

Wen Hongen Memorial Stele Unveiled Yesterday; Coinciding with the Third Anniversary of His Death; Mayor Reported on Mr. Wen's Career 114

Yesterday was the third anniversary of the death of the late Director Wen Hongen of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau. Mayor Wu, in memory of the late Director Wen's meritorious service to public security, ordered the Municipal Police Bureau to build a memorial stele for Mr. Wen in the bureau's central courtyard. It was completed a few days ago, and the unveiling ceremony was held yesterday. His family and friends also held the third anniversary commemoration. All parties presented wreaths, which were placed around the stele, and a portrait of Mr. Wen was hung. The ceremony began at 8:30 a.m. Among the participants were Mayor Wu, Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau, Director Li of the Health Bureau, Deputy Director Zhao of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, local gentry and merchants Huang Yanpei, Zhu Shaoping, Zhu Yinjiang, and hundreds of staff members and branch directors of the Public Security Bureau. Mayor Wu presided over the ceremony and reported on Mr. Wen's life experience, saying that the late Director Wen was a revolutionary party member who firmly believed in the Three People's Principles, obeyed his superiors, and was loyal to his duties. During the Northern Expedition, he fought in more than ten provinces and districts, and his vanguard reached Machang, making him the first to overthrow the Northern Warlords. When he took office as the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, after the January 28th Incident, he appeased the people, stabilized the local area, and worked diligently day and night. The city gradually recovered its old appearance, and his merits were undeniable. Therefore, he died of overwork. Colleagues and friends of the Public Security Bureau, recalling his past achievements, raised funds to build a memorial stele, which is of profound significance and worthy of emulation, etc. Subsequently, Su Liping, the chief secretary of the Public Security Bureau, delivered a speech on behalf of Director Cai, saying that the memorial stele of the late Director Wen has been erected in the square behind the main hall of this bureau. We should admire it day and night and learn from the virtues of obedience and honesty of the late Director Wen, implement national laws, and consolidate local security, so as not to betray the original intention of establishing the stele. Then, Mr. Huang Yanpei gave a speech saying that the late Director Wen had made contributions to the local area, and the establishment of the memorial stele was the public opinion of all the citizens of the city. He respectfully expressed his utmost respect as a citizen. Finally, Wen Huazhou, the younger brother of the late Director Wen and the chief of the regiment, gave a reply expressing his gratitude. After the ceremony, a group photo was taken and the attendees dispersed.

Incidents of Ships in Distress on the Yangtze River; Dehe Collided with the Riverbed at Wuhu; Shengping was Violently Hit by a Large Tugboat 118

Dehe's Rudder Chain Broke: The Dehe, owned by British Jardine Matheson & Co., is a regular liner on the Yangtze River with a deadweight of 3,770 tons. This time, it came down from Hankou to Shanghai, carrying many goods and passengers. The Yangtze River water level has been receding rapidly in recent days. The water level between Hankou and Jiujiang is only 9.7 feet according to the water gauge, and the draft is 13.6 feet. The Anqing water gauge is 8.4 feet, and the Wuhu water gauge is only 5.8 feet, with a draft of 10.4 feet, making it extremely difficult for larger Yangtze River ships to navigate. The Dehe arrived in Wuhu yesterday, and its rudder mechanism collided with the riverbed due to the low water level. The Dehe tried hard to pass through this shallow water area, causing the rudder chain to break and the ship to become immobile, stuck in the river. The situation was very bad. The shipowner urgently sent a telegram to Shanghai for help. The company received the report and immediately telegraphed the Xianghe, which has a shallower draft, to rush to the rescue. Yesterday afternoon, another telegram was received stating that the Dehe could be towed back to Shanghai by the Xianghe, but this would be delayed by one day and it would not be able to enter the port until tomorrow. After the ship arrives in Shanghai, the broken rudder chain will have to be repaired, and the loss will be significant.

Shengping Suffered Damage: The Shengping, owned by the Shanghai Minxin Steamship Company, has a deadweight of 4,434 tons, a cargo capacity of 7,040 tons, and a draft of 24.2 feet. It is a very large ship. The ship is currently loading cargo in the outer sea. Yesterday, Minxin Company received a telegram from the captain of the Shengping, stating that the ship was violently hit by a large tugboat near Tumpat Port on the Malay Peninsula, causing a hole to be punched in the outer hull. Only temporary repairs can be made at this time. The details of the loss and the circumstances of the accident have not yet been reported to Shanghai by the shipowner.

Doctor of Literature Cao Shanxiang Sentenced for Two Counts of Fraud; Fine of 200 Yuan to Be Enforced 121

Cao Shanxiang, a native of Ningbo with a Ph.D. in Literature from the University of Michigan in the United States, had a friendly relationship with Sheng Qingcheng, a native of Wukang and the director of the Hudong Hospital on Yangshupu Road. He once told Sheng that he was a classmate of Shi Ying, the mayor of Nanjing, and could arrange for a contract to handle the cleaning affairs of the capital city. Sheng immediately gave him 1,000 yuan for expenses. However, after Cao obtained the money, he disappeared without a trace. At the end of last year, he defrauded Luo Zhenting of 3,000 yuan on the pretext of seeking a position as a bureau chief. Recently, Cao was detained by the French Concession police for another case and brought to the Second Special District Local Court for interrogation. After the Xinzha Police Station learned of this, they found that Sheng had filed a lawsuit against Cao for defrauding him of money, and the First Special District Local Court had issued an arrest warrant. Therefore, they sent detective Ye Yushan to the Second Special Court to transfer Cao to the First Special Court for detention. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, Judge Pan Zhenyang opened the court to summon Sheng Qingcheng and Luo Zhenting, who had been defrauded, and brought Cao to court for questioning. Qian Xunjiu, the lawyer of the police station, explained the case and presented the confession of the defendant in the police station regarding his relationship with Sheng. He said that the defendant's confession was intended to discredit Sheng and Luo, who had accused him of being a "falling dog." Subsequently, Luo and Sheng explained the circumstances of being defrauded by Cao. When questioned, Cao denied the fraud, only admitting that he had borrowed the money from Luo and Sheng, and that they had all reconciled. He also hired lawyer Zhu Honglie to defend him. After the interrogation, Judge Pan immediately announced the judgment that Cao Shanxiang was guilty of two counts of fraud, each with a fine of 150 yuan, and the enforced fine was 200 yuan. If he was unable to pay the fine, he would be required to serve labor for one day per two yuan. He was also ordered to return 800 yuan to Sheng Qingcheng and allowed to provide a 200 yuan security bond.

Lawsuit Involving Promotion of Secret Mark Coupons and Suspension of Interest Payments; China Industrial Bank Should Pay Fuyuan Interest; Initial Trial Has Been Judged, But Defendant Appeals Again; Case Concluded After Interrogation, Judgment to Be Announced on the 16th 124

Shen Guangyan, the manager of the Shanghai China Industrial Bank, was previously sued in the civil court of the First Special District Court by Shi Hongdong, the manager of Fuyuan Silver Company, for non-payment of interest. Lawyer Qu Qian was engaged to file the lawsuit. The grounds for the lawsuit were that the defendant wanted to promote its bank notes and entered into a contract with the plaintiff, Fuyuan Silver Company, on April 22, 1933, in accordance with the prevailing practice of secret mark coupons among banks in Shanghai.

400,000 Yuan

For a term of five years, the plaintiff paid a large amount of printing fees according to the amount received and made every effort to promote the coupons, so that the agreed amount was fully circulated in the market. The defendant also paid the interest due in two installments each year, with an interest passbook as proof. Initially, the matter was handled on schedule and according to the agreement, without any objections. However, the defendant, citing the government's announcement of

Legal Tender Policy

Claimed that the aforementioned interest would be paid up to November 3 of the same year, and that the interest thereafter would be paid only when the formal contract was terminated. The plaintiff argued that Article 7 of the contract with the defendant stated that "The validity period of this contract is limited to five years. In the event of special circumstances, Fuyuan will be notified by public letter, and the contract will only be canceled after Fuyuan's consent." It can be seen that the cancellation of the contract requires the consent of both parties. Even if there are special circumstances,

Fuyuan's consent

Is still required. Therefore, the plaintiff had to file a lawsuit with your court. Subsequently, an out-of-court settlement was reached, and the defendant paid the money in full. The case was then withdrawn. On June 21 of this year, the time to pay the installment for the first half of this year arrived again. After repeated reminders, the defendant continued to delay. The plaintiff entrusted lawyer Qu Qian to send letters to urge payment, but to no avail. In order to protect its rights, the plaintiff had no choice but to file a lawsuit, requesting the court to order the defendant to pay 5,600 yuan in national currency.

Initial Judgment

The defendant should pay the plaintiff 5,600 yuan in national currency, and the litigation costs should be borne by the defendant. However, the China Industrial Bank refused to accept the judgment and, through lawyer Shan Yuhua, filed an appeal with the Second Branch of the High Court. Yesterday afternoon, Presiding Judge Han Zuzhi, accompanied by judges Zhang and Yu, took the seat and conducted a joint hearing. Witness Jin Lingyun testified. Subsequently, the arguments began. Lawyer Shan Yuhua, representing the appellant, requested the court to overturn the original judgment and dismiss the plaintiff's claim in the first instance. Lawyer

Qu Qian stated

That the appellant's grounds for appeal attacked the contract submitted by the appellee for not meeting the term of years. However, the contract submitted by the appellee was indeed for five years, and there were no signs of alteration. It was also stamped with the seal of Deputy Manager Jin Lingyun, who had the authority to enter into the contract, and there was no doubt about it. Therefore, it should be legally effective, and the appeal should be dismissed. The appellant should also bear the litigation costs of this instance, and the first instance judgment should be maintained and declared provisionally enforceable in accordance with Article 454 of the Civil Procedure Law. The court will render a judgment on the case on the 16th.

Assassination at the Intersection of Shi Tong Road: A Police Officer Killed, Sustaining Four or Five Knife Wounds to the Head and Face; His Service Revolver Also Snatched by Thugs 127

Dong Chuansheng, a police officer of the Northern Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, a 29-year-old native of Songjiang, previously served at the Shiliupu Branch in Nanshi. He was transferred to the Northern Railway Station Branch two months ago. He was known for his diligence and integrity, highly regarded by his superiors. However, at around 1:30 AM yesterday, while Officer Dong was on duty at Post No. 16, located at the intersection of Shi Tong Road and Zhongxing Road, he was suddenly attacked by a group of thugs wielding knives and axes, who inflicted four or five wounds to his head and face, resulting in his immediate death. His body collapsed on Zhongxing Road. A rickshaw puller named Shi Wanqing, who was passing by, noticed the body and reported it to the police officer at Post No. 14, who then reported to the branch. Director Liang of the branch personally led a team of senior officers to investigate. They found the surrounding area of the post and the seat inside were covered in blood. It is believed that while the officer was on watch, the thugs launched a sudden attack. Officer Dong resisted with all his strength, but eventually succumbed to his injuries. The officer's service revolver was also stolen. Only a felt hat left behind by the assailants was found at the scene, covered with numerous fingerprints and blood stains. Director Liang was extremely enraged after the inspection, stating that such thugs dared to openly kill public servants with weapons within his jurisdiction, showing utter disregard for the law. He has ordered a strict investigation to apprehend the culprits and bring them to justice. He has also reported the incident to the headquarters and requested the local court to conduct an autopsy. It is reported that the deceased is survived by a wife and a five-year-old daughter. According to Officer Dong's colleagues, he had no known enemies. It is suspected that this tragedy occurred because the thugs intended to steal the officer's firearm, and when the officer resisted, he met with misfortune.

Nie Guizhi, a Woman from Yushan, Accuses Xi Ehan of Abandonment; She Fled the War to Hangzhou and Was Introduced to Him as a Concubine; Now Abandoned, She Demands 30,000 Gold Yuan for Living Expenses 128

Xi Ehan (also known as Laichun), a wealthy Suzhou merchant residing in Shanghai, is over seventy years old and owns considerable property in Shanghai. Recently, Nie Guizhi, a thirty-year-old woman from Yushan, Jiangxi, hired lawyer Qian Yuan to file a complaint with the First Special Court's Criminal Division, accusing Xi of abandonment and demanding 36,000 yuan in civil damages. The gist of the complaint states that the plaintiff lost her father at a young age and lived with her mother. In [month missing] of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], the plaintiff fled the war to Hangzhou, where she was introduced to the defendant. The defendant boasted about his wealth and comfortable life, proposing to take the plaintiff as a concubine. The plaintiff, seeing that the defendant was elderly but had a dignified demeanor, readily agreed. They then engaged in sexual relations and soon came to Shanghai, where they lived together at No. 30, Lane 6, Jishan Lane, East West Huade Road. For two years, their relationship was harmonious. In February of last year, the couple returned to Yushan to visit the plaintiff's mother. The defendant returned to Shanghai first and urged the plaintiff to return. In September of the same year, the plaintiff came to Shanghai with her mother. However, in April of this year, the plaintiff

Returned to Her Hometown with Her Mother

And came to Shanghai in July. Unexpectedly, the defendant refused to take her in, effectively abandoning her. The plaintiff argues that the defendant's behavior of starting and then abandoning the relationship constitutes the crime of abandonment under Article 293 of the Criminal Code and should be prosecuted according to the law. In addition, she is filing a civil suit, demanding monthly living expenses of 100 yuan for a period of thirty years, totaling

Thirty-Six Thousand

Yuan. The court granted the request and ordered a summons to be issued. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng presided over the hearing in Criminal Court No. 8. The defendant, Xi Laichun, did not appear. The plaintiff's lawyer, Qian Yuan, stated that the defendant is a man of considerable means and that his residence is at No. 21, Mashi Road, Hangzhou, and he also owns a villa in Qingdao. He requested that the hearing be rescheduled. Judge Huang adjourned the case to the afternoon of the 20th of this month for further questioning of the defendant, Xi Laichun.

Land Acquisition for Heping Road: Property Owner Objects; Liu Xiang, a Lawyer, Sues the Court and Orders the Public Works Bureau to Compensate; Mediation Fails Yesterday, Formal Lawsuit to Follow 130

Lawyer Liu Xiang, courtesy name Jiren, previously owned a house located outside the Old West Gate on Zhaojiabang Road, now renamed Heping Road, at the streetcar turning point. The Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau planned to widen this section of the road and needed to acquire more than three zhang of his land. He considered the handling unfair and the losses too great, so in December of the 18th year of the Republic [1929], he submitted a petition to the Public Works Bureau requesting a change. The Public Works Bureau replied on December 13th of the same year, stating that the widening of roads and acquisition of land in the city would be handled in accordance with the "Temporary Regulations for Road Construction and Land Acquisition Fees," and that there was no

Undue Favoritism or Discrimination

Regarding the gains and losses of properties on both sides of the road. The request to change the route was related to the finalized plan and could not be approved. Liu then filed an administrative appeal with the Shanghai Municipal Government, which was rejected. Liu appealed again to the Ministry of Interior, which also upheld the Shanghai Municipal Government's decision. Liu, dissatisfied, filed a lawsuit with the Executive Yuan last year. Because Shanghai's administrative litigation, with the Public Prosecution Office as the main body, was unprecedented, his property tenant, Yu Nankui, also participated in the lawsuit. The main points of Liu Xiang's plea were: (1) The

Road Width

Was already stipulated to be 20 meters, so it should not be illegally expanded beyond 20 meters. (2) The original road system plan did not explicitly state where special widening was required, and the area was not particularly prosperous or have entertainment venues. A width of 20 meters would not obstruct traffic. The so-called plaza was merely an excuse by the Public Works Bureau. (3) According to Article 15 of the Land Expropriation Law, land expropriation should go through a negotiation process, which refers to whether the land should be slightly acquired and how many dimensions should be acquired. The Public Works Bureau

Did Not Negotiate

Which was clearly illegal. The defendant's official reply clarified that negotiation only referred to land prices, which was a misunderstanding. (4) Suzhou widened the Gongxiang Road, and some people requested reducing the width. The Shanghai United Transportation Station also temporarily suspended construction due to land acquisition issues, indicating that land acquisition plans could be altered to safeguard the interests of the people. He requested that the original decision and original disposition be revoked and that the road width be changed to 21 meters. Yu Nankui's

Reasons for Participating

Were roughly as follows: The participant leased the plaintiff's land in the 18th year of the Republic [1929] to establish the Hu Nan Food and Entertainment Company. The Public Works Bureau's expropriation of land beyond 20 meters hindered reconstruction. Dongmen Road has heavy traffic, but the road width is only 38 feet. Heping Road should not be further expropriated beyond 20 meters. The participant suffered indirect losses and therefore participated in support. After the court notified the Ministry of Interior to respond, they stated that (1) The Municipal Government announced the road width within its legal authority. The

Enlargement of the Plaza

To increase the area at road intersections was still within the scope of its authority and did not conflict with the Municipal Organization Law. (2) Negotiating the land price was part of the expropriation process and could be handled according to law. The people had no right to oppose the authority of the administrative agency. (3) The cases of Suzhou widening Gongxiang Road, reducing the width, and temporarily suspending construction of the Shanghai United Transportation Station were changes made by the competent authority and were different from this case. After reviewing the arguments of both parties, the court stated that the municipal government directly under the Executive Yuan,

Expropriating Land

When undertaking public works, in addition to the expansion of public roads stipulated in Article 10 of the Land Expropriation Law, which allows the competent authority to make its own decision when demolishing people's houses, should prepare a project proposal with a map and submit it to the Ministry of Interior of the National Government for approval and announcement, as clearly stipulated in Articles 8 and 9 of the Land Expropriation Law. It can be seen that the road widening case was originally a public work. The required land, in addition to other methods of directly purchasing it from the landowners, can be expropriated according to law, but must follow the

Clearly Defined Order

To handle. In this case, the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau believed that it was necessary to acquire more than three zhang of the plaintiff's land to widen the road. The plaintiff argued that the acquisition was excessive and lodged an objection. The original disposition rejected the plaintiff's request, stating that the land acquisition would be handled in accordance with the "Temporary Regulations for Road Construction and Land Acquisition Fees." However, Article 3 of the "Temporary Regulations for Road Construction and Land Acquisition Fees" stipulates that all land acquisition for road construction shall be handled in accordance with the Land Expropriation Law promulgated by the National Government. The court found that the original disposition authority did not

Present for Approval According to Law

The land acquisition case. The eastern road system of the Hu Nan district, approved and announced by the Municipal Government, was originally a road improvement plan. Since it was necessary to demolish people's houses, Article 2 of the Land Expropriation Law could not be applied. Before approval by the legal authority, it was difficult to consider that there was a basis for expropriation. Furthermore, Article 2 of the Shanghai Municipal Road Widening Regulations states that all buildings that obstruct the road alignment should be taken in at once during reconstruction according to the alignment. Also, Article 3, which states that property owners follow the

Alignment and Take In

The land, the Municipal Government should pay the full amount of compensation in accordance with the regulations. This provision can only apply to those who agree to the purchase, so there is no need to go through the expropriation process. It does not mean that the land expropriation procedure, which is already legally prescribed, can be changed by separate regulations. The conclusion is that, based on the above, the actual receipt of compensation is equivalent to a consensual purchase. If the landowner objects to the acquisition, they can only follow the Land Expropriation Law. After reporting to the authorities, if the rights cannot be obtained through agreement, a

Expropriation Review Committee should be organized to discuss and decide. In this case, the plaintiff

Had Objections to the Land Acquisition

If the original disposition authority considered that it was necessary to acquire the land according to the prescribed plan, it should have reported to the Municipal Government in accordance with the provisions of the Expropriation Law, which would be proper. It was illegal to simply reject the application. The decisions of the administrative appeal and the second administrative appeal were both inappropriate and should be revoked. As to whether there was a need to build a square on the land in question and how much to acquire, these were all within the scope of the expropriation plan. Since it had not been approved and announced, the plaintiff's request to determine that the road width was 20 meters was

Irrefutable

However, the original disposition authority did not complete the legal procedures for land acquisition. The plaintiff's accusation of illegality was not without reason. Therefore, the court ruled that the Municipal Public Works Bureau should report to the Municipal Government and follow the procedures stipulated in the Land Expropriation Law. Now Liu Xiang is holding this judgment and has repeatedly urged action without success, so he has applied for mediation in the Shanghai District Court, ordering the Director of the Public Works Bureau, Shen Yi, to compensate for the loss of 20,652 yuan. Yesterday, the judge opened the court. Shen Yi delegated Hu Tingji (who previously measured Liu's land) as his agent. According to Liu Xiang's statement, he was not notified at the time, but rather notified of demolition. This was Hu Tingji abusing his power for personal gain. Hu said the defendant should be the Ministry of Interior and there was no need for mediation. Therefore, the mediation failed, and a formal lawsuit will be filed.

National New Pharmaceutical Industry Federation Holds Second National Congress Yesterday; Over 100 Representatives Attended; Chairman Xu Xiaochu Delivers Speech; Resolved to Establish a Raw Material Import Cooperative, etc.; Two Associations Held a Luncheon, and the City's New Pharmaceutical Industry Held a Banquet in the Evening 132

The National Federation of New Pharmaceutical Industry Associations held its Second National Congress yesterday. At noon, the city's New Pharmaceutical Manufacturing and Pharmaceutical Factory Associations hosted a luncheon for representatives from various provinces and cities. The meeting continued from 2:00 PM onwards to discuss proposals and resolve key issues such as cultivating pharmaceutical talents, organizing a raw material and new drug import cooperative, and cracking down on improper and exaggerated drug advertisements to maintain the industry's reputation. Attending Representatives

The National Federation of New Pharmaceutical Industry Associations held its Second National Congress in the city yesterday. Representatives from the Municipal Party Department, Wang Yucheng; the Social Bureau, Fan Aiwei; the Health Bureau, Tao Qingan; the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Sun Mingqi; the National Physicians Association, Xu Nali; the Pharmacists Association, Qiu Shaobai; the Chinese Pharmaceutical Society, Liu Buqing; the standing director of Wuzhou Pharmacy, Lu Qingxue; and representatives from various provinces and cities such as this city, Hankou, Kaifeng, Yunnan, Yantai, and Chongqing: Xu Xiaochu, Zhou Bangjun, Yuan Hesong, Jia Chengyuan, Zhu Ruichen, Zhu Yuquan, Chen Xingwu, Xu Bincai, Liu Buqing, Chen Shenghai, Xu Xiangsun, Tu Kunhua, Shi Zhifu, Tu Kaizheng, Gu Kemin, Pan Ruitang, Xia Xishi, Chen Yuzhang, Yao Junzhi, Gao Peiliang, Zhang Keyong, Xu Chao, Xiang Caiwu, Zhou Mengbai, He Zikang, Zhou Shiluo, Ding Jianyan, Sun Deruo, Guo Shaolou, Zhao Shengbin, Zheng Runlin, Chen Zhongge, Xie Younan, Ma Xinquan, Teng Curong, Wang Shaopu, Liu Peien, Pan Ziliang, Yuan Fengzhou, Shu Changjian, Hu Zhaoxiang, Lu Shiru, Yang Fabing, Tan Yigeng, Fan Wenwei, Chen Shengchao, Zhang Hanxiang, Wu Shaojiu, Zhang Yueqian, Chai Peifeng, Zhang Ji[name missing], Wang Xiangwu, Qian Pinfang, Wang Hepu, Chen Xiaoping, Xiang Runquan, Shen Yinxin, Tian Zuomin, Cheng Qianyuan, Wei Ziyi, Kong Jichuan, Mao Huixian, Tu Haoquan, Huang Ziyin, Luo Bowen, Jin Shaoan, Yu Bingnan, Zhou Yunsheng, Liu Yanchen, Luo Jiufu, Pei Zishan, Peng Zhongyi, Lin Hesheng, Xu Shousun, and over 100 others. The Presidium included Xu Xiaochu, Zhou Bangjun, Yuan Hesong, Tu Kaizheng, and Xu Guansu.

Chairman's Speech

After the meeting began, Chairman Xiaochu delivered an opening speech, stating that the association's various affairs over the past year have been reported in detail and need not be repeated. However, in short, whenever members have difficulties, the association will do its best to assist them. Whenever the government issues relevant medical and pharmaceutical regulations, the association will promptly forward them. This is the duty of the association. The new pharmaceutical industry is not merely a business or a pursuit of profit, but is closely related to public health and national health. Therefore, the solidarity of our industry is not only to seek mutual survival and prosperity, but also to benefit society and the country. Since its establishment, the association, recognizing the lack of pharmaceutical talents in our country, has established pharmaceutical training courses. Recognizing the lack of widespread pharmaceutical knowledge, it has published the New Pharmaceutical Monthly to broaden publicity. Whenever the government has measures related to public health and national health, the association is happy to support them. Today, the association gathers representatives from all over the country to work together with one heart and one mind, express their opinions, and see that the association's affairs will be developed even more in the future. At this time of serious national crisis, I hope that our industry will always uphold the heart of saving people is saving ourselves, and benefiting people is benefiting ourselves, to jointly seek the welfare of the industry, benefit society, and fulfill the national duty. Then the organization of the association will not be in vain, and a century of great planning can be expected. Then, representatives from the Party and government gave instructions and presented work reports, which were extremely detailed.

Resolved Various Cases

The association continued its meeting at 2:00 PM, chaired by Xu Guanchu, to resolve various cases. (1) The pharmacy training institute should continue to enroll students so that pharmaceutical talents can be cultivated to meet the actual needs of society. (2) Please stipulate the curriculum and regulations of pharmaceutical training institutes in various places to seek unified treatment. (3) Please add correspondence courses to the pharmacy training institute to facilitate the widespread cultivation of pharmaceutical personnel. (4) Urge the Ministry of Health to promptly promulgate remedial measures to address the shortage of pharmaceutical students in order to alleviate commercial difficulties. The above cases were discussed together and it was resolved to pass them in principle and hand them over to the executive committee for handling. (5) Request the Ministry of Finance to specify the types of smuggled drugs. (6) Submit to the Ministry of Health a modified method for purchasing narcotic drugs to meet supply and demand and facilitate convenience. (7) Submit to the Ministry of Health for approval to allow pharmaceutical students to sign and sell narcotic drugs. (8) Legitimate drug merchants who legally sell narcotic drugs should be given legal protection by the government. (9) Request the Ministry of Finance to delete the item of new drugs from the types of imported goods inspected. (10) Request the Ministry of Health to quickly establish regulations for narcotic injections and their production and transportation methods to benefit medicine. (11) Request the Ministry of Health to allow pharmaceutical students to sign and certify proprietary medicines and apply for inspection. (12) Suggest that the Ministry of Health purchase the medical narcotics sealed up by the national industry in accordance with orders to alleviate commercial difficulties. The above cases were resolved and passed. (13) Organize a raw material and new drug import cooperative to control quantities, reduce costs, avoid being manipulated by foreign merchants, and use research and imitation to prevent loopholes. (14) Investigate the sales quantities of foreign finished medicines and raw materials in pharmacies throughout the country. (15) Unify prices. (16) Maintain the reputation of the industry, report and punish the manufacture of counterfeit drugs. (17) Restrict foreign firms from directly selling goods to users to avoid disrupting market prices. (18) Crack down on Chinese people who run new drug businesses and call themselves foreign merchants and products of a certain country to emphasize national dignity. (19) Establish a chemical testing laboratory to inspect imported raw materials to emphasize product quality. (20) Actively raise funds to build a guild hall to expand business. (21) Crack down on improper and exaggerated drug advertisements to maintain the reputation of the industry. (22) Investigate colleagues nationwide, find ways to connect, and publish a directory. The above cases were passed in principle and handed over to the executive committee for consideration and handling. After the discussion, Yuan Hesong delivered a closing speech and announced the adjournment of the meeting.

Gu Chuntao, Director of Yong'an Silver Company, Arrested; When a Company Cannot Pay Off Debts, Directors, etc., Should Be Responsible for Repayment; Gu Granted Bail of 1400 Yuan for Further Questioning 133

Yong'an Silver Company was organized by the famous anti-Japanese general Li Du (resident of No. 316 Jing'an Villa, Jing'an Temple Road) and Wang Jiazhen, Zhang Zilian, Qian Youju, Peng Baohui, Lin Kanghou, Gu Chuntao, Mo Dehuan, Lin Zhenhu, Jiang Bohan, Ou Jiancheng, etc., who served as directors, managers, and other positions. On December 12 of the following year, they filed a joint lawsuit against the above-mentioned directors in the First Special Court. The court ruled that if the company could not pay off the debts, the defendants would be responsible for repayment. After the judgment became final, it could not be enforced because the addresses of the defendants were unknown. The court issued an arrest warrant. The creditors learned of the whereabouts of Gu Chuntao, one of the directors, the day before yesterday afternoon, and notified the court. The bailiff and the police went to Gu Chuntao's residence in Baxianqiao and arrested Gu, sending him to the Second Special Court for detention. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Executive Judge Song Xizhong presided over the hearing in Criminal Court No. 8. Wang Zhuoyuan, a respected lawyer, appeared on behalf of the creditors, requesting enforcement. A lawyer defended the defendant. After questioning in court, it was decided to grant Gu bail on the condition that he would be available for questioning at any time, and the hearing was rescheduled for 2:00 PM on the morning of the 14th.

Central Bank Inspection Report 138

The 308th Inspection Report on the Central Bank's Exchange Certificate Issuance Reserve states: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the bank's exchange certificate issuance amount and reserve funds. The 208th inspection was held at the bank's Issuance Bureau on November 7, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of exchange certificates issued is 30,911,4175 silver dollars, including 27,224,4335 silver dollar certificates and 3,686,9840 subsidiary currency certificates. The total amount of exchange certificate reserves is 30,911,4175 silver dollars, including 20,225,5675 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 50,843,075.48 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance headquarters, branches, and sub-branches, and 11,141,2599.52 silver dollars stored in other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 10,685,8500 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold exchange certificates issued is 400,9630.07 customs gold units. The total amount of customs gold exchange certificate reserves is 400,9630.07 customs gold units. This reserve includes 7,926.290 ounces of pure gold, valued at 51.68, totaling 400,9630.07 customs gold units. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve should be at least 60%, with the remainder guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. November 9, 1936, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Li Fusun; Supervisors, Xie Mengjun, Bei Sun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Ji.

Meeting Minutes of the Barber Industry Association 140

The Shanghai Barber Industry Association held its fifth executive meeting yesterday afternoon. The attending committee members were Xin Yuling, Zhu Mingqing, Hu Yucai, Li Yongcheng, Zheng Renheng, Chen Shengxi, Jin Wanquan, Zhou Hongde, Xia Mingqing, Wang Chunbo, and Ji Zhaolin. Chairman Xin Yuling presided over the meeting, followed protocol, reported on proposals, and made the following suggestions: (1) The association's finances have been tight for a long time. According to the previous meeting, temporary advances will be collected from all committee members to prepare for operational activities. It was resolved to instruct the General Affairs Department to quickly prepare for the collection from the committee members. (2) The city's barbers have not yet uniformly joined the association. It was resolved to place an advertisement on the cover of the Shen Xin newspaper, requesting all barbers in the city to fill out application forms and fulfill their obligations to the association. Monthly donations will be temporarily divided into four categories. (3) The city's Chamber of Commerce and Education Association sent a letter requesting an investigation into the need for vocational training among Shanghai trade associations. It was resolved to instruct the Director of Organization to handle it. (4) The city's Party Department sent a letter instructing the introduction of subscriptions to the Anti-Drug Monthly for promotional purposes. It was resolved to instruct the Director of General Affairs to handle it. (5) The association has recruited Zhang Bairen as a temporary secretary on a voluntary basis. What should be the term limit? Please make a decision. It was resolved that he will serve voluntarily for two months initially, and the policy will be determined later. All the above five items were unanimously approved and the meeting adjourned.

Chinese Medicine Science Society Creates a Prize for Excellent Manuscripts 143

The Chinese Medicine Science Research Society, located at 16 Xiangxin Lane, Aierjin Road, has published five issues of its Scientific Medical Journal. In addition to selections by members of the society, the works are carefully crafted masterpieces from the medical community across the country, and have been praised by medical circles at home and abroad. Subscribers and readers are spread across remote counties and cities. In order to improve the content of the medical journal, enhance the high-level medical knowledge provided to readers, and encourage interest in submissions, the society has created a prize for excellent manuscripts. Those who rank in the top ten will receive silver shields and other prizes. Detailed rules are being drafted jointly by the society's General Affairs and Editorial Departments, and will be implemented regularly. This is truly an innovation in the medical publishing industry.

Weather Report 144

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong and the surrounding areas are clear and cold, with strong northwest to north winds. The Yellow River basin is windy and without a fixed direction. The middle and upper reaches of the Yangtze River are cold, with intermittent cloud cover. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River and the East Sea and Taiwan are experiencing strong northwest to northeast winds. There is a cyclone in the southeast of Japan, with adverse weather conditions due to a hurricane moving northeast. The center of the hurricane reached within approximately 120 miles of 31 degrees latitude and 143 degrees east longitude at 2 PM. The wind force is unknown. Also, the highest temperature in the city within the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was 68.4 degrees, and the lowest was 46.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 66.6 degrees and the lowest was 47.7 degrees.

General Overview of Industrial and Commercial Changes in Shanghai, July and August This Year. An Overview of Industry and Commerce in Shanghai (38) 146

— Edited by China Credit

(1) Bank of China Establishes New York Branch: The establishment of this branch was the result of negotiations between Mr. Chen Guangfu, Executive Director of the bank, and the US Department of the Treasury during his visit to the United States. With the establishment of the Sino-US Monetary Agreement, further cooperation between the banking sectors of China and the United States became necessary. Therefore, the Bank of China decided to establish a branch in New York, and invited Mr. Wang Zhengxu and American Mr. Bozes to be the managers of the branch. This marks the beginning of the direct participation of Chinese banks in the American market.

(2) Hua'an Commercial Savings Bank Undergoes Forced Liquidation: The bank was initiated by Hu Chunxiang, Zhang Danru, and others. Preparations began in the winter of 1932, and the shareholders' meeting was established in May of the following year. It officially opened on July 4, with a fully paid-up capital of 50 million yuan, operating commercial and savings businesses. Mr. Yu Shicheng served as the Chairman of the Board, and Mr. Hu Chunxiang served as the General Manager. Since its opening, business was initially thriving. In the first year, deposits reached 1.3 million yuan. In recent years, due to the impact of the economic downturn, many loans could not be recovered on time, and since the opening of the China Communications Savings Department, most depositors withdrew their deposits and transferred them, leading to a decline in business and stagnation of capital. The organizers convened a temporary shareholders' meeting on June 30, but it was adjourned due to insufficient attendance. Unable to do otherwise, in addition to rescheduling the shareholders' meeting for the 29th of this month, the bank moved its address from 271 Ningbo Road to 73 Ningbo Road, and reduced staff to save expenses. At the same time, it stopped accepting deposits and granting loans, focusing on liquidation matters. When the shareholders' meeting was held on the 29th, the board's proposal was passed, formally announcing the forced liquidation.

(3) Reorganization of Shanghai Silk Industry Commercial Savings Bank: The bank was founded on September 1, 1933, by silk industry leaders Wang Yansong, Luo Qinghua, and others. Initially, the capital was set at 500,000 yuan, but due to enthusiastic subscriptions, it was increased to 600,000 yuan. A five-story building was built on Hankou Road, and Mr. Wang Yansong was appointed as Chairman of the Board and General Manager. Later, due to the development of business, the original funds were still insufficient, so the capital was increased to 1.2 million yuan, and the bank joined the Shanghai Banking Association and the Shanghai Clearing House. Last year, the bank pioneered the acceptance bill system, which was highly valued by the financial community. Recently, due to the impact of the economic downturn, and because Mr. Wang was tired of his duties, there was a bank run. In order to revitalize the business, the bank's board of directors specially hired Mr. Lu Zidong, General Manager of Jiangsu Bank, to serve concurrently as the bank's manager, and the Bank of China, the Central Bank, and the Bank of Communications fully provided capital to revitalize the business.

Sports News

French Concession Hard Court Tennis Singles: Ma Anquan and Li Buzu Win Finals Berth: Ma Defeats Coracha and Naffan Yesterday: Doubles Also Feature Chinese Team Ma-Zhou against Li-Hu 147

Since the French Concession Hard Court Tennis Championships began on October 31st, most of the finals berths have been decided as of yesterday. Except for one mixed and one women’s doubles semi-final match, which will be resolved on Sunday morning, the men’s singles and doubles finals week are occupied by Chinese players, which is the most glorious page since the French Concession hard court tennis began. There are no matches today or tomorrow, and the finals will be held separately on Saturday and Sunday. Tickets are all one yuan. The current situation of the championships is as follows:

Men's Singles: Li Buzu vs. Ma Anquan

Men's Doubles: Ma Anquan, Zhou Guanjun vs. Hu Xuguang, Li Guofan

Women's Singles: Mrs. Kremlinoff vs. Mrs. Hales; Women's Doubles: Mrs. Moore and Mrs. Lambros vs. (Miss Tavans and Mrs. Kremlinoff or Miss Metri and Mrs. Hales); Mixed Doubles: Mrs. Moore and Defoe vs. (Mrs. Kaito and Forbes or the Kremlinoffs).

Ma Anquan Defeats Coracha

After Zhou Guanjun and Wang Shuzi successively lost in the right half of the men's singles, only Ma Anquan was left to hold the fort for the Chinese players. Yesterday, Mr. Ma had to play two matches in a row. The first match was against the Portuguese star Coracha, which was held at 1:30 PM. Coracha is known as a tough opponent, but he was in poor condition yesterday. Except for one service game won by Coracha in the second set, Ma easily won the rest, ending the set 6-1. In the second set, Ma broke Coracha's serve, and Coracha broke Ma's serve in the next game, tying the score at 1-1. After that, Ma won two more games in a row. Coracha managed to win a game with his serve in the fifth game, but then slumped again. Ma, on the other hand, was unusually spirited and ended the set 6-2. In total, they battled for fifteen games.

Ma Wins Quickly Against Kanafaro

After defeating his strong opponent Coracha, Ma Anquan faced Kanafaro in the semi-finals at 3:30 PM. Mr. Ma continued his momentum, using long shots and short drops with great skill, making Kanafaro exhausted. Ma had the serve in this match. Except for the third game of the first set, which was broken by Kanafaro, resulting in a win for Kanafaro, the rest were like crushing dry weeds. Ma quickly ended the set 6-1. In the second set, Ma was even more courageous, winning a shutout set and defeating Kanafaro to advance to the finals week.

Shen Zhen Loses to Li Bizu

Shen and Li are outstanding players among the Chinese. They have defeated foreign players in the past few days. Yesterday's match was the key to winning a finals berth. Both sides showed their skills, fighting a fierce battle. In the first set, Li initially showed the power of Pu Ma, winning three games in a row. Shen, an old general on the battlefield, was not flustered and calmly responded. As a result, he turned defeat into victory. Li was stunned, winning only one game and losing 4-6. In the second set, Li Bizu carefully fought back and achieved victory. In the final set, Li’s courage was not exhausted, and he defeated his strong opponent 6-2 to win a finals berth.

The Hu-Li Team Luckly Wins a Finals Berth

The team of Hu Xuguang and Li Guofan was supposed to meet Kocher and Mastot in yesterday's match. Kocher and Ma are outstanding among the foreign players. They had a tough battle against the Kremlinoffs to win the semi-finals. Although Hu and Li are brave, it was unknown who would win against these two. Unexpectedly, luck came beyond expectations. Kocher and Ma were late yesterday, and according to the rules, they were deemed to have forfeited the match. Thus, Hu and Li won a finals berth without any effort.

The Married Couple Succeeds, Easily Takes Zhou-Yan

The Chinese mixed doubles team Yan Jingjiang and Zhou Shejun met the strong Kremlinoff couple yesterday. Mr. Kremlinoff’s shots were sharp and quick, and Mrs. Kremlinoff was steady and pleasing. Yan and Zhou were often trapped. The Kremlinoffs were active in the first set, and although Yan and Zhou tried to counterattack, they did not succeed. Soon, the score became 4-1. The Kremlinoffs continued their efforts and won the set 6-3. Zhou Guanjun performed very well in the second set, creating a 5-5 tie, which was temporarily encouraging. The Kremlinoffs attacked fiercely, and Yan and others fought to the death. In the last two games, the competition was extremely fierce. Eventually, Zhou and Yan lost again due to slightly loose coordination.
