Ticket Sales Will Begin Soon

Regarding the performance by world professional tennis player Tilden Barnes in Shanghai on the 20th of this month, a contract was signed on the eve of Tilden's departure from Shanghai (the 6th). The remuneration is still a 4-6 split, with Tilden getting 60% (the reason for the previously reported 3-7 split was due to other complications; the actual split is 4-6). Tickets are divided into three categories: 5 yuan, 3 yuan, and 2 yuan. The 5 yuan tickets are for the first to third rows, numbered, totaling 540 seats. The 3 yuan seats are from the fourth to tenth rows (formerly the 5 yuan seats), unnumbered. The 2 yuan seats are the former 3 yuan general admission seats. Tickets will be available for sale around the 14th. However, even if all tickets are sold, only about 8,000 yuan can be obtained, which is at least 2,520 yuan less than the previous performance. Although Tilden and others will only receive 6,216 yuan in national currency for this performance, accounting for 60% of the total income of 10,367 yuan, equivalent to about 1,800 US dollars, they are extremely interested in our country. It is said that because of his advancing age, he will not be able to endure long sea voyages, and it will be difficult to fulfill his wish to revisit our country in the future. However, he is deeply impressed by the high level of tennis enthusiasm in our country, and wishes to have a second opportunity to work together. Therefore, he has agreed with Barnes to invite three more first-class professionals next summer to come to Shanghai again, and then continue to Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, Beijing, and other places.

In addition, tennis enthusiasts in this city plan to invite Tilden to perform in Beijing after his performance on the 20th. They are currently in contact with Tilden by telegram and with Tilden's agent in Shanghai, but have not yet received a reply. It is expected that the President McKinley, General Pershing, and Customer Wheel will depart for the United States on the 24th of this month and will arrive in San Francisco on the 13th of next month, only four days later than the Lincoln Wheel, and will be able to make it in time for the Christmas holidays. Therefore, it may be possible to invite Tilden to agree to participate in a performance match hosted by Chinese players.

Privately Funded Students Studying in Japan Must Obtain Certificates of Study Abroad and Submit Them to the Study Abroad Management Agency for Verification; Otherwise, the Ministry of Education Will Not Recognize Their Qualifications 164

In recent years, the number of Chinese students studying in Japan at their own expense has increased sharply. Many of them have followed the regulations of the Ministry of Education to complete the study abroad procedures. However, there are also quite a few who have gone abroad without obtaining a certificate of study abroad, or who have obtained a certificate of study abroad but have not reported to the Office of Supervision of Students Studying in Japan. In view of this, the Ministry of Education has reiterated its previous order and notified all schools above the junior college level that the qualifications of students studying in Japan at their own expense must meet the standards stipulated in the Ministry's Regulations on Studying Abroad. Their study abroad expenses and all their behaviors must be reliably guaranteed, approved by the Ministry, and issued with a certificate of study abroad before they can go abroad. After arriving in the country of study, they must submit the certificate of study abroad to the study abroad management agency in the country for verification and registration within two weeks. Otherwise, the Ministry of Education will absolutely not recognize it. Therefore, before going abroad, privately funded students studying in Japan must obtain a certificate of study abroad from the Ministry and report to the study abroad management agency after arriving in the country of study before their qualifications for studying abroad can be recognized.

Zhang Runruo Lectures on Sound Bin: "Support the Leader" and Self-Reliance for National Salvation (2) 167

2. Regarding the relationship between leaders and the people, we must first recognize the connection between the nation and the individual, national strength and self-reliance, leaders and the people, and centripetal force and automatic power.

Speaking of the connection between the individual and the nation, the nation is an organism, and the individual is the cell that constitutes the life of the nation. My body is the cell of the nation, and my life is a part of the nation. On the one hand, the individual and the nation have an inseparable, interdependent, and unified connection; on the other hand, they each have their own special functions. As citizens, we should each do our best and fulfill our responsibilities to strive to meet the overall needs (Note 3).

Speaking of the connection between national strength and self-reliance, the development of the nation is based on the excellence of the people's intelligence, morality, and physical fitness. Without the development of the people's intelligence, morality, and physical fitness, there is no possibility of substantial national strength. We must contribute our individual intelligence and talents to the nation and gather the economic, moral, spiritual, and physical strength of the people to create a strong national strength. Therefore, the prerequisite for strengthening national strength depends on whether the cells of the nation's life, that is, every citizen, can fulfill their national duties to strive to meet the overall needs and to strive to improve the nation's functions (Note 4).

Speaking of the connection between leaders and the people, and centripetal force and automatic power, the development of any ethnic nation must have two important conditions: on the one hand, the development of the concept of the nation; on the other hand, the self-awareness of national responsibility. The reason why the world's great powers can soar and advance rapidly is based on the promotion of these two historical forces. Human beings, in any era, must have two qualifications: on the one hand, as a member of the collective; on the other hand, as an independent self (Note 5). From the former point of view, we need the centripetal force to support the leader; from the latter point of view, we need the automatic power of the people.

The reason why the Chinese nation has today's decline is due to the disconnection of the above-mentioned various positions. On the one hand, there is a lack of a unified and centripetal national concept, so we are selfish, harm the public for personal gain, do not abide by discipline, and cannot unite. On the other hand, we are accustomed to decadence and do not think about revitalizing. The general public is dominated by the inertia of history since the Jin, Wei, and Six Dynasties, which has formed a decadent nature of mechanical extremes, completely disappearing the individual's sense of responsibility to the nation and the automatic power to society (Note 6).

Therefore, today's work of national salvation should be planned and taken care of in both aspects. On the one hand, we need a wise leader; on the other hand, we should focus on the training of the people. Leaders are very important, but the relationship between leaders and the people is like the tip of a pyramid and the bottom line. We must have a healthy and large public as its foundation, so that we can rely on it without falling. Even if the leader's ability surpasses the group, he is not three heads and six arms, and he is still beyond his reach. At least we need people with motivation as his backing, and then we can complement each other and achieve twice the result with half the effort. Otherwise, it is like a row of axles that are broken and dilapidated. Even if the machine in the front of the car is powerful, it cannot leap forward.

The reason why the Soviet Union after the revolution has today's construction achievements and national strength development is not only due to the strength of their ruling class, but also the result of their first leaders training and educating the people. The basic driving force for the revival of Germany after the war is also the inherent spirit of perseverance, fortitude, hard work, and self-improvement of their people. The rise of Hitler was caused by the times, and the development of the National Socialist Party (allowed to be the norm in German history (Note 7). Moreover, as after Mussolini ruled Italy, he was always deeply concerned about the danger of "the government ceasing when the person dies." Therefore, he was very concerned about the training of the people. Those who do not know think that Mussolini's success is based on Machiavelli's hegemony, but they do not know that Mussolini's ability to promote Italy has other underlying driving forces. Mussolini believes that the decline of a country is due to the spirit of the people. Therefore, on the one hand, he vigorously reformed the political institutions to strengthen the centripetal force, and on the other hand, he worked hard to cultivate the spirit of the people to inspire their inherent virtues of struggle, hard work, thrift, generosity, courage, enthusiasm, and sympathy, so that the people of the whole country can be powerful and inherit the great historical mission of glorifying the nation's life.

Here, we should know that the success of a leader is not accidental or achievable by luck. We must have the people of the whole country able to exert their automatic ability as the backing of the leader before we can engage in long-term struggle and hold the left coupon of victory. If the people of the whole country have a mentality of dependence and do not change their decadent habits, and let the leader fight alone without supporting him, then the effect of seizing the door will be twice the result with half the effort. Even if there is success, it will be difficult to maintain for a long time. Learning from the past is the teacher of the future. Therefore, if we truly love the leader, the method of supporting the leader is not in false praise, nor in temporary excitement, but in the down-to-earth, hard-working training of the people of the whole country and the cultivation of the people's motivation, so that the people of the whole country, regardless of scholars, farmers, workers, businessmen, men, women, old and young, can all be in their own positions, recognize their tasks, and complete their great duties to the country and society, so as to reduce the leader's hard work and share the leader's heavy responsibilities, and concentrate the automatic power of the whole people to help the leader and be used by the leader. Then the leader and the people will be like fish in water, complementing each other. In this way, the leader's hard work and the people's efforts can be balanced and advance together to jointly complete the historical mission of national salvation and revival with hardship and hardship.

Peace Student Union. Promote One-Day Movement 168

(Central News Agency, Baoding) The city-wide "One-Day Movement" initiated by the Student Union has been generally approved in principle after Shi Neiying and Hao Zhongqing contacted various parties on the 9th. However, there are some researches on the use of the funds. Teachers and staff of various colleges and primary schools donated one day's salary and it has been implemented on the 10th. Middle school students have implemented cost reduction, and primary school students are free to donate. The Chamber of Commerce has scheduled to convene industry associations on the 12th to discuss. The citizens plan to ask the Public Security Bureau for assistance. According to Shi Neiying and Hao Zhongqing's separate statements to reporters, the purpose of the "One-Day Movement" is to fulfill national obligations, absolutely free, and without restrictions. Only 13 representatives from colleges and universities attended the meeting on the 7th. The rumor that more than 100 people attended is not accurate.

Separate orders to county education bureaus and various vocational schools to comply with the order from the Ministry of Education received by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education that the Ministry has repeatedly sent personnel to inspect the status of vocational schools in various regions. Four Schools Hold Anniversary Celebrations 170

Hujiang University Shanghai Hujiang University was established six years before the founding of the Republic of China and has reached its 30th anniversary. The school's development has progressed with each year. Various facilities are quite large. Graduates who have served the community have reached thousands and are well-known. The school is scheduled to hold a large-scale celebration from the 20th to the 22nd of this month. The commemorative ceremony will be held at 3:00 p.m. on the 21st. At the same time, an exhibition will be opened to welcome alumni, students, parents, and guests from all walks of life.

China Women's Middle School China Women's Middle School on Lin Yin Road, West Gate of this city, was founded by Wang Xiaoying. Yesterday was the school's third anniversary. A celebration ceremony was held in the morning. More than 500 teachers and students attended. The principal reported on the school's history. It was decided that representatives of teachers and students would give speeches. A recreational performance was held in the afternoon.

Huiling Middle School Huiling Middle School in Xinlonghua, this city, has been established for 17 years. The school held its 17th anniversary celebration on the 10th. A ceremony was held in the morning. Chairman of the Board of Directors Chu Fucheng was invited to the school to give a speech. In the afternoon and evening, there were recreational performances, and the Peking opera rehearsal by the Fudan Alumni Association, which alumni of the school joined, was very exciting.

Patriotic Women's School The Patriotic Girls' Middle School on Jiangwan Road in Mubu will celebrate its 25th anniversary on December 5th this year. Fifteen people including Yin Songya, Hu Zuoxia, and Yang Minghao were specially appointed as members of the preparatory committee. A general meeting of alumni will be held on December 6th.

Zhejiang Library Woodblock Printing Books 171

Zhejiang Literature and Books at a 30% Discount This Month The Zhejiang Library on Hangzhou University Road is the successor of the Zhejiang Official Book Bureau and continued to carve book plates in the early years of the Republic of China. It preserves 150,000 plates and sells more than 400 kinds of national academic masterpieces. It has always been known for its exquisite engraving and proofreading. Due to local relations, there are many Zhejiang literature and Zhejiang people's collections. These ancient books have always been sold at real prices. It is learned that the library will hold a Zhejiang literature exhibition from November 1st to 15th. In order to give preferential treatment to visitors and those who love ancient learning, all books will be given special discounts (wholesale and agency sales are not included in this preferential treatment). All lead-printed books will be discounted by 20% (such as the Siku Catalogue, etc.), and woodblock-printed books will be discounted by 10%. In order to promote Zhejiang literature, books related to Zhejiang literature and the collections of Zhejiang sages will be discounted by 30% during the exhibition period, even below cost, in order to promote the circulation of books. For example, the large-format Jiang Tongzhi, 120 volumes, is sold for only 22.4 yuan after the discount. The woodblock-printed Zhang Taiyan Series, 24 volumes, is sold cheaply for only 7.288 yuan. Postage is added. The illustrated book catalog published by the library is a huge two-volume set with detailed content and precise categories and examples. The original price is 6 yuan, and it is specially priced at 2 yuan in November (postage is added). In addition, the library's two periodicals are also being discounted by 20% for half a month. Wenlan Journal (quarterly) aims to promote Zhejiang culture and review academics. The original price is 2 yuan a year, now it is 1.6 yuan. "Library Outlook" monthly magazine aims to introduce new knowledge and assist the general harm. It has been published for a year, and the special issue of Volume 2, Issue 1, has just been released, with a variety of content and many updates. From Volume 2, the Shanghai Magazine Company will be entrusted with the general distribution. The annual subscription price is 1 yuan. Subscriptions at the library are also discounted by 20% before the 15th (subscriptions in Shanghai are not included in this case). This special price is for a very short period. The deadline for Hangzhou City is the 15th of this month, and the exhibition for other places will be extended to the end of November. However, the two periodicals will be closed by the 15th. Detailed lists are printed and will be sent upon request.

Securities. Public Debt Prices Suddenly Rise --Up 7.5 Cents to 1.35 Yuan-- 173

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange experienced an unexpected surge in market prices, and the trend never softened. It may be too early to say that it is a sign of improved times, or that there is a new agreement with the United States. In fact, the short covering and the full-day buying on the 5th were all related. Most of them are still speculative in nature. From the opening to the closing yesterday morning, the prices rose without falling. The opening price rose by 3 to 6 cents, the settlement price rose by another 3 cents, and the afternoon rose by another 1 to 3 cents. The closing price still rose by 2 to 3 cents. The most active buyers were those who bought the full day on the 5th. The others, such as No. 33, 34, 47, and 53, also followed suit and took consistent actions. The chips on the market suddenly felt scarce. Although No. 4 and No. 11 actively sold, they turned long again. The depressed situation of the past few days suddenly unfolded. Since the interest payment, this is the highest record. Although there is still hope for continued negotiations in the future, the bulls are already crowded, and a pullback must be prevented. As a result, the market prices rose by 7.5 cents to 1.35 yuan. The total turnover was 16,085,000 yuan. The results of the price increases and decreases are compared in the table on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan).

Finance. The Gold Bidding Market Was Quite Active Yesterday. Although the Result Fell by One Dime, the Trend Was Still Stable. 174

The gold market was active yesterday because large buyers were eager to supply. The market situation hovered for half a day. In the early morning, the overseas silver market showed that the British market rose and the US market was flat. The standard gold bidding price was listed, and it was reduced to 1159.8 yuan. The over-the-counter preparatory transaction opened, retreating to 53.5 yuan to 4 yuan. Qiafeng Yonglai entered, rising to 4 yuan. The morning opening was a low market. Although there were many sellers after the opening, the large buyers also had a strong appetite, and some who covered their shorts were immediately pulled up. Yarn Flowers This Month, Yarn and Spot Prices are Equalized Buyer Interest Suddenly Decreases - Most Have Started Swapping - 177

The yarn market is weakening, and the situation is soft. The reason is that the price of November yarn has been equalized with the spot yarn price, and those going long are less interested. A certain factory has 4,000 bales of open interest, and most of them probably have yarn to deliver, so the November contract alone fell. However, most of the bulls abandoned January and switched to December and January contracts, indicating that the bulls have no intention of taking delivery. Also, today is the anniversary of the Premier's birthday, and the market is closed for one day.

Many Sell Marked Yarn When Prices are High

The marked yarn market opened. Due to the bulls swapping positions in the current month, the momentum weakened. However, the December 1st date is relatively tight, but some are taking the approach of selling on rallies because the price has reached a high level. It is found that most of the bulls are still tightening their positions because their inventory is not high and they do not want to give up, so the power of consolidation is very strong. As a result, the marked yarn for the current month closed lower than the previous day by 16 jiao, and the distant month fell 4.5 jiao. When the market opened in the afternoon, the market condition for the current month was very weak. Because the yarn factory strike is not difficult to resolve, the bulls began to swap positions, and the market situation worsened, breaking the 30-yuan mark. The distant month dragged down the decline. As a result, the current month contract fell another 1.3 yuan from the morning closing price, and the distant month fell 5.6 jiao to 1 yuan. It is found that 2,100 bales of Mingde were sold, 1,900 bales of Zhenda, 10,000 bales of Changyu, 1,650 bales of Yihe, 3,100 bales of Runkang, 1,800 bales of Dachang, 1,750 bales of Yuda, 1,050 bales of Gengfeng, 2,250 bales of Dachangcheng, and 1,150 bales of Changfeng. 2,250 bales were bought by Hexing, 2,500 bales by Ruida, 1,300 bales by Shenji, 2,950 bales by Taichang, 2,650 bales by Yichang, 1,350 bales by Tongfeng, and 950 bales by Changji. The highest and lowest market prices for the day are listed on the left.

Spot Yarn Sales Feel Good

It is found that various gangs bought a total of 1,215 bales throughout the day, and the selling price was average. The thread price rose by 2 yuan. The amount bought by each gang is as follows:

Labor Strike Can Be Resolved Cotton Market Resists Shorts Strongly 178

The cotton market rebounded. Because it had fallen for days, it prompted profit-takers to cover, so the market tightened and the market rebounded. However, British cotton production increased and the market was weak. Some still shorted on rallies.

Marked Cotton Reacts and Rises

The marked cotton market opened. The near month was still weak because American cotton fell all the way and people were not encouraged. However, the far-term prices rose because profit-takers covered. The market turned up after the second trading session. However, there was crowding from various sources. As a result, each month rose 2.5 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. When the market opened in the afternoon, it was expected that the yarn factory strike could be resolved soon and the market turned bullish. Short covering activity increased and the market fought back. As a result, the near month rose another 5 fen to 2 jiao compared to the morning closing price, and the far month was flat. It is found that 7,800 dan of Taichang were sold, 7,500 dan of Changfeng, 5,400 dan of Yikang, 7,600 dan of Yuanyu Chang, 1,200 dan of Yukang, 2,400 dan of Zhenda, 1,200 dan of Tongfeng, 4,500 dan of Xiecheng, 2,800 dan of Jinkang, 1,500 dan of Dachang. 5,400 dan were bought by Tongji, 5,900 dan by Hengyi, 3,800 dan by Yuda, 2,900 dan by Jinchang, 4,200 dan by Hexing, 2,100 dan by Gengfeng, 5,600 dan by Fengtai, 3,400 dan by Wang Taixing, 3,100 dan by Yongda, 4,200 dan by Mingde, 2,500 dan by Renfeng, and 2,300 dan by Changhe. The highest and lowest prices and closing prices for the day are listed on the left.

Spot Cotton Mill Offices Are Still Clear

Spot cotton consumption is normal. Mill needs are not lacking. There are 1,050 bales of Yaohua and 950 bales of Tonghua from various sources.

American and British Cotton Markets Both Weak 179

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened, and the market was weak. Each month fell 10 to 13 points. There were not many transactions. Prices fell due to poor news from Liverpool, domestic and foreign bulls liquidated, and cotton farmers hedged. Except for limit-down buying, there was a lack of demand and prices fell. The near term was stable, and the distant term had hedging. The spot cotton base was firm, and the cloth market was active and strong. Fellow traders were watching the domestic publication and exports. It is said that a large cooperative has advised its trustees to sell, which has gradually weakened market sentiment. Before the close, bulls liquidated and hedging started again, and market prices weakened further. It is estimated that spot prices fell 10 points, and futures fell 10 to 15 points. British spot cotton fell 15 points, and futures fell 12 points. Indian cotton rose because of reports of rain and European exporters buying Oomra. Bull liquidation was offset by short covering. It is estimated that Pinggor fell 0.75 to 1.5 rupees, Oomra fell 1 rupee, and White Karachi fell 1.5 rupees. The original telegram is on the left. (10th telegram)

According to a telegram from Mumbai, the opening forecast for the 11th is White Karachi at 217.5 rupees, down 0.75 rupees, Oomra at 196.5 rupees, down 1.25 rupees, and Pinggor at 157.5 rupees, down 0.75 rupees.

Three Grades of Yarn Rise and Cotton Falls 180

Osaka telegram on the 11th, the three grades of futures yarn rose 2 jiao to 2.1 yuan, the near month was 231.9 yuan, and the distant month was 208.9 yuan. Cotton futures fell 5 fen to 2 jiao, the near month was 65.55 yuan, and the distant month was 65.85 yuan.

Piece Goods Spot Cotton Cloth Gradually Feels Scarce 181

Yesterday, the trend of the cloth market was still good. Although domestic and foreign cotton markets have declined unanimously in recent days, the spot yarn sales are strong and prices are firm, the thread price has risen by more than 7 or 8 yuan, the strike wave in yarn factories has gradually expanded, and cotton cloth has risen due to the spot shortage. Yesterday, Dong goods fine twill rose another 5 fen to 1 jiao per piece, and fine twill and fine cloth from this factory also rose (about 2 jiao per piece). However, printed straight tribute, crepe, satin, printed flannel and other goods are sold the most lightly, and the selling market is difficult to revive. The selling market of Shilin cloth and colored twill followed the rise of grey cloth, but it is also difficult to keep pace with white goods because sales are not smooth. Customer sales are only good for the Yangtze River gang. The demand in other sales areas is weak. Because the market price has entered a high level, the selling price in various places is not good, and actual sales have shrunk. Yesterday, the Hankou and Changsha gangs had a very strong demand, and handled more than 300 pieces of fine cloth, fine twill, straight tribute thread, woolen cloth, coarse cloth, flannel and other goods.

Grains Foreign Wheat Plunges Long Position Flour Bulls Emerge Frequently Non-industry Speculators Also Wait and See Result: A Uniform Drop of Two to Three Fen 182

Yesterday, the flour market had strong selling pressure and seemed to be trending downstream. Foreign wheat prices, from Chicago and Canada, each fell by a little over 1 jiao to a little over 3 jiao. Liverpool fell by three-quarters. In general, people are hopeful that foreign wheat prices will approach. Speculative bulls emerged one after another, and non-industry speculative stomachs waited and did not advance. Therefore, after the morning closing, the market went downstream step by step, and near and far months fell by as much as 3 to 4 fen. However, spot sales are still worthy of maintenance, and there is still a gap between the price of foreign wheat, so customers take the opportunity to buy, and the intention to buy is even more intense. By the afternoon closing, the situation had stabilized. If foreign wheat prices are calm in the future, the market may be able to maintain support for the time being.

Spot Goods Outlets Stall Futures Wheat Selling Vigorously 183

Yesterday, the futures wheat market saw an even sharper decline. After the market opened in the morning, foreign wheat prices were uniformly lower, and spot wheat outlets stalled. People were generally weak. Long position holders gave up, and new short trading was also active. For a time, selling pressure was vigorous, and the market opened and fell step by step. By the time of the close, the decline had slowed slightly as flour prices turned steady. As a result, near and far months fell by 5, 6, 7, and 8 fen compared to the previous day. Spot wheat, due to dwindling stocks, sellers are unwilling to let go, and factories are trying to make repairs, so the situation remains strained, and no transactions have yet occurred.

Customer Xian Rice Market Still Has No Good Signs 184

Yesterday, there was still a strong arrival of customer Xian rice, and the market still lacked good signs. However, customer sales are still active and the market is still able to support itself. Only the prices of goods below Zhongguan have a tendency to level off. Brown rice is still being actively handled by the Guangdong merchants and is relatively strong. It is estimated that 4,500 bags of Zhejiang, Hubei and Changsha brown rice were handled. The Guangdong merchants' demand for machine rice is very slack, except for rice, only 400 bags of broken rice were handled. Henan handled 600 bags of early machine rice. Xiamen handled 233 bags of machine oil. This merchant handled more than 2,000 bags of Xiang, Gan, and Taiwan machine broken rice. The market conditions are similar to the previous market.

River Rice Floods in Market Prices Ultimately Difficult to Recover 185

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of fifty or sixty merchant sources arrived, with more than 12,000 shi of goods in total. The sales market on this street feels even more sluggish. And the Qingdao and Yantai gangs continued to handle five or six thousand bags of Bo Dao and more than four hundred bags of thick new Japonica. However, its market conditions are difficult to maintain due to the large number of arrivals. As a result, the market price of thick and thin rice each fell by one jiao, and the supply and demand of Duyang Jian and Yin Bianyuan are similar, without honor or disgrace.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, thirty-two merchant sources arrived from the river, and the market demand was flat. The price of new Japonica was short by five or six fen, Bo Dao was short by another seven or eight fen, the price of Yang Du Bu Jian was short by three or four fen, and the price of Yin Bianyuan stood still. The customer's Jian demand was not good, and the price was flat and sluggish. Also, today is the Premier's birthday, and both the North and South rice markets are closed for one day to commemorate it.

Soybean Oil Cakes Rise Across the Board 186

The oil and soybean cake market has a correlative relationship, so when one rises, they all rise. Recently, the oil and soybean cake sales market has been active, and the Dalian market has continued to rise, causing the market sentiment to tighten uniformly. Yesterday, soybean cake was opened for 15,000 pieces of Dachang factory's spot and futures four-brand cake. Although the market price did not move, the factory's products are in high demand, and the selling price must be lower than other factories by two. According to yesterday's market, the factories tightened their positions and did not open, so the future market situation is expected to continue to rise. Soybean oil and raw oil rose another 2 jiao. The factory handled five carts of Che beans and two carts of Sipingjie beans. Other merchants handled eighty bags of Late soybeans and fifty bags of Shayellow. The market price rose by one or two jiao.

Oil Market Paraffin Wax Industry Negotiates Selling Price 187

The Shanghai Paraffin Wax Industry Association held an evaluation meeting at 10 am yesterday. More than ten representatives, including He Yinsheng and Fan Zonglin, attended. Mr. He was elected chairman. After the formalities, the chairman reported that the selling price should not change. After public decision, the selling price of each product is as follows: "Mingzhong" 22.2 yuan per load, "Zhongjing" 21.8 yuan per load, "Macheng" 20.02 yuan per Shanghai load, "Yakou" 124 yuan, "Mixin" 122 yuan.

Page 16

A Comprehensive View of New Paraffin Oil 188

The paraffin oil production areas are currently harvesting and pressing oil. Although the yields vary between regions, it is estimated that about 60-70% can be harvested. It is reported that Jingzhou, Yichang, and Zhiguo in western Hubei, Macheng in northern Hubei, and Jinshi in western Hunan all have more than 70%, while Jinlan, Wen, and Tai in Zhejiang are also between 60-70%. Only northern Anhui and southern Jiangxi are about 50% or slightly stronger. Only the old source areas of western Zhejiang, such as Chongde and Tongxiang, are the most soft, probably only a little less than 20-30%, and the production is not large, so there are more inferior grades and fewer superior grades. If calculated by the entire country, there are more superior grades and fewer inferior grades. The inventories in various places are not strong, but only thin. The Heben oil in western Zhejiang has 7-8,000 pieces of old goods. With so much inventory when new goods are about to be produced, this is unprecedented in the past ten years. Shanghai is close to it, and every time new goods are first produced, Heben is used as new goods to report because new oil from distant places arrives late, so Heben sales to Shanghai are the most unique during the first batch of new goods. Every year around the winter solstice, the oil workshops come to Shanghai to sell futures oil, and they can always be seen on the road. Now, due to the poor yield this year and high seed prices, it has been collected to about 6.5 yuan per stone, and the cost must be more than 20 yuan. Even the oil workshops dare not pre-sell, and considering the prices in various places, Heben oil is considered the most expensive. Those who handle it cannot calculate it, so they all intend to wait and see. It is speculated that the oil workshops will only sell a small number of new oil when it reaches 20 yuan, but the local merchants in this city are unwilling to accept it based on the price of Han oil, and it must be separated by one yuan. Because of this, the buying and selling parties have not been able to approach, resulting in a silent market.

Silk and Tea The Reason for the Sharp Rise in New York Silk Prices Good Impression of the Silk Market after the US President's Re-election Declining Inventory Prompts Speculators to Cover 189

Yesterday, the wind of rising prices for overseas raw silk was too strong, and New York was even more firm. After examining the reasons, according to those familiar with foreign situations, it is because US President Roosevelt was re-elected, and all industries are expected to recover. At the same time, the inventory of raw silk in New York is decreasing day by day, and the delivery of goods is still on the way, resulting in a temporary shortage of spot goods. In addition, the recent surge in Japanese silk is extremely continuous, which has prompted New York speculators to cover their shorts. Due to these factors, silk prices have risen day by day. It is estimated that yesterday, spot prices in Yokohama rose by 10 yuan, futures rose by 7 yuan, Japanese silk in New York rose by 1-2 points, Shanghai silk maintained the original price, Guangdong silk rose by 1 point, and exchange market prices rose by half a point to one point for near and far months. In Lyon, except for Shanghai silk A, which did not move, the rest of the silk products each rose by one franc. There was no lack of transactions in the local silk market. Jardine Matheson, Wing On and others still had strong demand. Unfortunately, various Western merchants closed for half a day due to horse racing, so silk transactions were slightly less. End of Wait 194

— Yunbo

During the Ming Dynasty, the Wokou pirates were extremely rampant, relying on their power to act unscrupulously, invading and harassing the coastal areas of our country. The provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang suffered the most severely. Consequently, many heroes who resisted the Wokou emerged, leaving behind many earth-shattering and moving historical events. People like Qi Jiguang and Yu Dayou became famous because of this. Hou Duan was also a hero of that time, but probably not many people know this name.

Hou Duan was a brave general from Jinshan County, Jiangsu Province. He practiced martial arts from a young age, so his skills were superb. It would be impossible for several hundred ordinary people to move him, let alone get close to him. He could truly be called a hero who could uproot mountains and carry tripods, a brave man with bronze muscles and iron bones.

One day, he was chatting with people in front of the yamen (government office) when someone said, "The warriors of ancient times always said they had the strength of a thousand jun (ancient unit of weight, approximately 30 pounds) in both arms. I wonder if that's true." Another person then said to him, "Brother Hou, we know you're strong, but we don't know exactly how much strength you have." Hou Duan, upon hearing this, looked at the stone lion weighing a thousand jin in front of the yamen and said, "I wonder if I can lift this stone lion." After saying this, he stood up, walked to the stone lion, bent down, and hugged the stone lion with both hands. First, he shook it a bit, then he straightened his body, and the stone lion left the ground and rested in his arms. He even carried it around the yard for a circle before putting it back in its original place. His face wasn't red, he wasn't panting, and he smiled as he asked, "How about that?" At this point, the onlookers were already dumbfounded. Their tongues were stuck out and couldn't retract; they couldn't even speak.

On one occasion, Hou Duan was riding a horse on the road. As he looked at the green mountains and clear waters, he couldn't help but think to himself, "Time passes quickly, but I haven't accomplished anything yet. If I continue like this, wouldn't I be wasting my bronze muscles and iron bones? I've been idle for many years; I wonder if my muscles and bones have weakened recently?" At this moment, he was passing under a stone memorial arch. He stretched out both hands, grabbed the horizontal beam at the top, and used his legs to squeeze the horse, exerting force upwards. This lifted both man and horse into the air, hanging there as if suspended, performing three "hangings." After a good while, he finally loosened his hands, allowing the horse's hooves to touch the ground, and then nonchalantly urged his horse on and rode away.

From somewhere, a white-browed tiger had appeared in the neighboring county of Nanhui, frequently coming out to harm people and livestock, frightening the local residents so much that they didn't dare leave their homes for days. Although the government had offered a reward for someone to capture it, several hunters who went to claim the reward were injured by the tiger, making its reputation even more fearsome. The people of that place were restless, unable to eat or sleep, and worried day and night. When this news reached Hou Duan's ears, he volunteered to go and kill the tiger, taking his sword with him. After a fierce battle, he killed the violent tiger, eliminating a major threat to the local area.

Although Hou Duan was so brave, he didn't have the opportunity to perform great deeds because no one recognized his abilities. He was just a garrison officer in Jinshan County.

At this time, the Wokou pirates happened to invade Jinshan again, bringing thirteen pirate ships and leading tens of thousands of men, with great momentum, surging towards the south of Jinshan city. When the scouts received this news, they immediately reported it to the county government. The officials in the government were all terrified of the Wokou pirates. Upon hearing this news, they were already out of their minds and didn't know what to do. They couldn't think of any way to protect the people, let alone muster the courage to resist. They were only concerned with their own lives and families, and fled one after another.

Hou Duan, being a righteous man, knew that defending the city and resisting the enemy was his duty and didn't want to escape. Moreover, this was a good opportunity for him to show his skills and establish his reputation, so how could he give it up? However, he was just a minor general with only a few hundred soldiers under his command, so his strength was very weak. The Wokou pirates, on the other hand, had a large force and great momentum. Furthermore, they were attacking with courage, making them unstoppable. The situation at the time was that the numbers were unequal, but he wasn't afraid at all. He led his troops out of the city to resist the enemy, stationing them in Yangjia Tuan, outside the east gate. He also moved the residents' food and supplies outside the city.

Just as they were preparing, the Wokou pirates' ships arrived. Hou Duan hurriedly rode his horse to the seawall to observe the situation of the Wokou pirates. At that time, the tide was receding, and the water near the shore was very shallow, so the Wokou pirates' large ships couldn't sail in and were anchored about a li (approximately one-third of a mile) away from the shore. They were launching small boats, preparing to transport troops to the shore. A pirate general dressed in red led the way, commanding the small boats, linking them together in a line, heading straight towards the shore.

Upon seeing this, Hou Duan turned his horse into the water and rode towards the small boats. After riding for a while, the water gradually became deeper, and the horse's belly strap was blocking the water, making it difficult for him to move forward. Hou Duan then jumped off his horse, drew his knife, and cut the belly strap, dropping it into the water. He jumped back onto his horse and continued forward. When he was about a hundred paces away from the small boats, he reined in his horse, drew his bow, and aimed an arrow at the red-clad pirate general. The red-clad pirate general was giving commands and was caught off guard. The arrow pierced his throat, and he fell to the ground. The Wokou pirates were shocked to see their commander suddenly fall to the ground, and their formation became disorganized. Everyone hurriedly turned their boats back and gathered around the large ships. After a while, they saw that Hou Duan was alone, so they added more troops and charged towards the shore again. Unable to resist them alone, he turned his horse back. On the way, he encountered a shepherd. Fearing that the Wokou pirates would chase after him because of his white horse, he borrowed a sheep from the shepherd and killed it, smearing the sheep's blood on the horse's body, turning the white horse into a red horse. This allowed him to safely return to Yangjia Tuan.

The Wokou pirates' purpose in invading was to plunder. Now that they had landed, they would naturally seize men to serve and work for them, seize women to satisfy their lust, and plunder property, preparing to return home fully loaded. They acted unscrupulously along the way, committing many atrocities of burning and slaughter, and performing various brutal and cruel acts. This forced the residents along the coast, especially those who were wealthy, to flee at the first sign of trouble. Those who remained to be slaughtered were just the poor. How could the Wokou pirates' desire for plunder be satisfied? They knew very well that cities were more prosperous places, with more people, thriving industry and commerce, and more comfortable daily necessities than in the countryside. Moreover, the granaries and treasuries were definitely full of food and wealth. Their focus for plunder was naturally still on the cities. If the cities were heavily guarded, they would still risk their lives to attack. Now that Jinshan city was offering no resistance, they would naturally occupy it without hesitation.

After the Wokou pirates occupied the city, most of their elite troops all went ashore, leaving only the old, weak, and disabled soldiers on the ships. They assumed that the soldiers were afraid and wouldn't dare to resist, so they only cared about raping, looting, and enjoying themselves temporarily, without any plans for defense or occupation. Hou Duan saw this weakness of the Wokou pirates and took advantage of their carelessness to lead his soldiers in a sneak attack on the pirate ships at night. He ordered the soldiers to bring sulfur, kerosene, firewood, torches, etc., to set the ships on fire when they got close. In an instant, the wind added to the fire's power, setting all the ships, large and small, ablaze. A red light illuminated the area as if it were daytime, turning the river's surface blood red. The soldiers guarding the ships either died in the fire or drowned in the water. Those who managed to escape to shore were killed by swords and knives. None of them escaped. By the time the Wokou pirates in the city received the news and came to put out the fire, the ships had already turned to ashes. From then on, the Wokou pirates were cut off from their return route and lost their reinforcements, leaving them in a difficult situation. They could only desperately defend the empty city, stationing a team outside the west gate to act as reinforcements, but when they came out of the east gate, their power was greatly diminished.

Seeing the Wokou pirates' weakened state, Hou Duan wanted to take the opportunity to wipe them out. He reasoned that if he allowed them to continue occupying the city, he would be failing in his duty to defend the country's territory. Moreover, if the Wokou pirates' reinforcements arrived, they would become even more ferocious and difficult to control. Therefore, he immediately led his soldiers to attack the city. He himself rode a white horse, wielding two swords, and rode along the city walls. He went to the south gate and saw that it was closed, so he couldn't do anything. He then rode his horse towards the west gate. The west gate was open, but the drawbridge over the moat had been destroyed. He was about to lead his troops across the river to attack when he looked back and saw that his soldiers had been left far behind when he rode his horse. However, a group of Wokou pirates stationed outside the west gate had already surrounded him, trying to capture him. He thought, "Enough, at this point, what am I afraid of? But simply fighting them is not worth it. As the saying goes, 'To catch bandits, first catch the leader,' and 'If you don't enter the tiger's den, how can you catch the tiger cubs?' I might as well rush into the city alone, kill them to my heart's content, and then rush back out of the east gate, which is closer." After thinking this, he backed his horse up a few steps, patted its head, and shouted, "Horse! Horse! You must try your best to jump over the river! Otherwise, you and I will both die!" The horse was truly clever, as if it understood his words. It jumped over the river. He was overjoyed and full of energy. He shouted loudly and charged straight into the city.

The Wokou soldiers in the city tried to capture him, but he slaughtered them like cutting melons and vegetables. Anyone who was grazed by his sword was wounded, and anyone who touched the blade fell to the ground. They couldn't stop him. Although Hou Duan was alone, surrounded by enemies, he charged left and right, as if he were in an empty place. However, there were too many Wokou pirates, and he couldn't drive them back. From morning until noon, the fighting continued without end. He felt hungry and tired, and he had suffered many injuries, so he didn't dare to linger. He had to cut a bloody path and flee towards the east gate.

Seeing that they couldn't stop him, the Wokou pirates came up with a clever plan. They used a whole bolt of coarse cloth, with dozens of people pulling on each end, and stretched it across the road, hoping to trip Hou Duan's horse. Hou Duan used his left-hand sword to lift the cloth and his right-hand sword to cut it, charging through. When he reached the east gate, he cut through the gate and rushed out. Unexpectedly, a team of soldiers with hooks was lying in ambush beside the gate, hooking him with long hooks. One of his arms was hooked. The Wokou pirates, seeing that they had hooked him, used all their strength to pull. Fortunately, Hou Duan was strong and couldn't be pulled. He struggled with all his might, tearing apart four pieces of his armor, broke free from the hook, and rode back, covered in blood.

He had charged into the city alone and killed many people. When they spoke of it later, they regarded Hou Duan as a divine general.

After Hou Duan returned to his camp after this great battle, he realized that one person's bravery couldn't wipe out the Wokou pirates. He gathered the remaining soldiers, trained the people, expanded the team, and prepared weapons and food. At the same time, he worked hard to train them, advocating the true meaning of saving the country and resisting the enemy. After his long-term training, his army became strong and powerful, completely different from before. Knowing that the time was ripe, he re-swore to lead the army to eliminate the Wokou pirates and launched a major attack on the city, easily defeating and killing the Wokou pirates. Those who scattered and fled were also killed or captured alive by the people in the surrounding villages. In the end, he completely annihilated the Wokou pirates.

Samuel Finley Breese Morse (1791-1872) 195

— Li Weiyi

-Inventor of the Telegraph-

Morse was a scientist and artist, born in Charleston, Massachusetts, USA on April 27, 1791. His father was a pastor. Morse entered Yale College at the age of fourteen. Under the tutelage of professors Day and Silliman, he developed a great interest in electricity, and as a result, he became famous in this field.

In his early years, he liked art more than science. Therefore, he studied with Washington Allston, one of the most famous artists in the United States at the time, and lived in England with him for four years. His achievements during this period were great. He returned to the United States in 1815, hoping that the government would appoint him to the task of writing history books, but he was unsuccessful. He only managed to get a job in Charleston doing portraits. Later, he went to New York and settled there. In 1825, he laid the foundation for the National Academy of Design in the United States and was elected as its first president. By 1827, his interest in electricity was revived. At this time, he studied electromagnetism with Professor J.F. Dana at Columbia College. However, his interest in art remained strong, and in 1829 he went to Europe again to study with his former teachers.

The year he returned to his country, 1832, can be said to be the time when he ended his artistic pursuits and began to concentrate on scientific research. On the deck of the ship returning home, one day he and several passengers were discussing electromagnetism. He suddenly seemed to have an inspiration and said: "If electricity can exist in any part of a wire, I believe that there is no message that cannot be transmitted through it."

From then on, he worked hard to study, and soon proved that electric current can travel along a wire to any distant place in an instant; and knew that if the line was broken, sparks would come out. He also discovered that sparks could represent part of a language, either letters or numbers; the disappearance of sparks could also represent another part of the language; if the existence or disappearance of sparks was prolonged, it could represent some other words; so letters could be easily created, and single words could also be expressed. After several days of work, he drew a rough draft of the necessary machine and showed it to the people on his ship.

Then, Morse worked hard in poverty for several years before completing his invention. First, in 1835, he invented the "relay" that he had long wanted to supplement, so that the current that had weakened after passing through a long distance in the wire could be restored again. In 1836, he completed a working telegraph machine. On September 2, 1837, in his room at New York University, he took out his machine for several friends to see, and installed 1,700 feet of copper wire here. The result of the experiment was very satisfactory, and it stimulated the interest of several brothers named Vail, copper and iron craftsmen from New Jersey, in studying electricity. From then on, they often interacted with Morse in practical applications.

Morse requested the government to give him a patent, which was approved on September 28, 1837. Soon after, he petitioned Congress to allocate a subsidy to him to cover the cost of purchasing materials, so that the telegraph could be applied in practice. The petition was accepted by the Commerce Committee, which gave him a good word in its report to Congress, but Congress delayed the matter and did not allocate the subsidy to him. So he ran to various European countries to seek patent rights, but did not succeed in any way. In England, his request was rejected; France granted him a patent and gave him some subsidies, but the amount was too small to be useful. Russia thought his invention was useless and did not allow him to use it. A year later, he had to return to New York.

It was not until February 23, 1843, that Congress passed his long-shelved petition and gave him a subsidy of $30,000. He set up a telegraph between Baltimore and Washington. In May of the following year, the two places communicated for the first time, and the results were very good. Morse was very happy and unconsciously sent out this sentence: "What Hath God Wrought!"

Morse and several of his former colleagues who had worked together on the research obtained patent rights and soon organized a company to lay telegraph lines all over the United States. From then on, his career developed day by day and received praise from governments and people all over the world. Austria, Belgium, France, Russia, Turkey, Sweden, the Netherlands (now the Netherlands) and several other small countries sent representatives to give him bonuses because of the convenience and widespread use of the telegraph in their countries, collecting a total of 400,000 francs.

Morse not only had immortal success in telegraphy, but also befriended Mr. Daguerre in Paris and studied photography with him, achieving considerable success. He was the first person in the United States to use silver plate photography (photography that coats silver salts on copper plates). He also invented submarine cables. He died in New York on April 2, 1872, but his career is immortal.

Publishing Industry

The Current Situation of the Chinese Publishing Industry and the Path it Should Take in the Future 196

— Dachuan

The rise and fall of a country's culture is fully reflected in its publishing industry. When we look at the advanced countries of the world, the quantity of their publications can determine the stage of their cultural progress. Countries such as Russia, Germany, Japan, the United States, Britain, and France show this significant phenomenon. Looking back at our own China, its cultural backwardness and the scarcity of its publications are truly shameful and leave us with the regret of being far behind. I remember foreigners saying that China's current culture is still that of 18th-century Europe, which makes us even more ashamed.

What is the current situation of the Chinese publishing industry? What kind of culture does it reflect? Talking about these issues really feels vast and boundless, because the scope involved is so large, and the internal situation is so complex that it cannot be fully explained in just a few hundred words, just as the world says, where to start talking about the "Twenty-Two Dynastic Histories"!

When observing the current stage of the Chinese publishing industry, people naturally focus on its actual phenomena as the starting point for their observations and discussions. This article will also be based on this key focus and the surrounding environmental conditions to give a rough description, and briefly discuss my humble opinions on the current causes of the weakness of the Chinese publishing industry and the new path it should take in the future:

(1) The purchasing power of the intellectual class is weak. Due to the current economic panic, both urban and rural areas are in a state of recession. The suffering is even greater among the intellectual class. Due to the pressure of life and the loss of employment, their economic power to purchase publications is gradually weakening. I have investigated many people who like to read very much. Three or four years ago, they could still buy books and newspapers worth dozens of yuan every year, but now they can't even afford books worth a few yuan. Economic pressure has caused them to lack spiritual food. This is certainly the most painful thing for intellectuals, and at the same time, it is a major crisis for the publishing industry.

(2) The content of publications lacks essence. From the perspective of the Chinese themselves, there seem to be quite a few publications in China now. On average, there are four or five new books and two or three hundred magazines published every month. Newspapers all over the country are not included in this list. However, looking at their content, there are very few new ideas or refined discussions. This is not an exaggerated statement. In fact, most of the people currently engaged in compiling and publishing publications have empty personal life experiences and shallow knowledge. When they write, they either cut and paste other people's works or plagiarize foreign people's opinions, piecing them together into chapters. The beginning and end are inconsistent, the content is chaotic and scattered, and the writing is dry and obscure. This kind of situation is a common disease among general authors, and those who suffer from it severely will carry the virus into the publishing industry. It is a pity that young readers, like lost sheep, are unknowingly harmed. Therefore, there are still many people who are not optimistic about the new culture and shake their heads when it comes to the current publishing industry, sighing at the decline of culture and the many stillborn publications. The many morbidities of the publications themselves can also stimulate a small part of the demand for readers.

(3) Competing to print ancient books and reprint for profit. There is a special phenomenon in the current publishing industry, that is, the various bookstores in Shanghai, the so-called cultural center of the country, are competing to print ancient books from past dynasties. The times are moving forward, but their publications are mostly turning backward. The louder the call for popularizing education, the more printed materials they specialize in supplying for the appreciation of the leisured class. There are very few systematic reorganizations like the "Historical Series of Internal Turmoil and Foreign Disasters in China" of the Shenzhou Guoguang Society recently. We are not opposed to reprinting ancient books, because this also has its background and the decisions of the current environment. Why not do it when you can revive the inherent culture without paying manuscript fees? There is also a very strong trend of secretly printing and reprinting pirated versions. These trends were not uncommon in Beijing, Tianjin, and Kaifeng nine years ago, but now this trend is still very rampant in Shanghai. This kind of thing certainly violates the publishing law and harms the interests of authors and their publishers, but because of the low prices of pirated versions, they are very popular among general readers. Even in the case of school textbooks, the number of pirated books is not small. However, the paper is too poor and there are too many typos, which also harms readers. In addition, the rampant printing of various ancient and modern chivalrous and romantic novels, selling them at low prices, and making them popular all over the country and deep into the interior, is the most profitable speculative business in the publishing industry, but it does not do any good for the entire publishing industry, because their goal is to seize money, and they are fundamentally indifferent to the evolution of culture.

Reading Notes (Continued) 197

The book is divided into eight chapters. The first chapter is an overall discussion, the second is on administrative organizations, the third is on central administrative organizations, the fourth is on local administrative organizations, the fifth is on autonomous administrative organizations, the sixth is on the legal relationship of officials, the seventh is on administrative acts, and the eighth is on administrative remedies. Each chapter is further divided into sections and subsections. For example, regarding various organizations, it explains their meaning, system, classification, characteristics, powers, etc. Each item is then analyzed in detail, with a clear and well-organized presentation. Furthermore, it constantly refers to the country's draft system as a reference, making it easy for people to understand and discuss. It truly achieves a level of simplicity and completeness, making it effortless to read.

Moreover, if we want to deeply understand any kind of system, it is best to compare it with similar systems. The book also pays attention to this point. For example, regarding administrative law, it points out three differences from administrative science in terms of purpose, basis, and conclusion. For delegation and agency, it notes four differences. Officials and public servants also have four points of difference. Regarding disciplinary penalties, it compares them with criminal punishments and lists seven differences in terms of basis, object, cause, purpose, effectiveness, executing agency, and scope of discretion for explanation. Regarding administrative regulations, it points out several differences from administrative orders. Regarding the distinction between appeals and petitions, it points out three differences. The difference between administrative litigation and civil litigation also has three differences. All of these involve repeated comparisons to make understanding more thorough.

In addition, the book lists the theories of various schools for each legal system, but it is not broad and without a guiding principle. For example, regarding the distinction between public law and private law, there are theories of relationship, theories of law, theories of interest, etc., and finally, it points out that the theory of interest is more complete. The standard for distinguishing between public legal persons and private legal persons includes the theory of purpose and affairs, the theory of state organs, the theory of group power, the theory of state relations, and the theory of personality differences. Finally, it says that the theory of personality differences is appropriate. Regarding whether one should obey an order that conflicts with laws and regulations, it mentions legal, order, and compromise theories, and says that the compromise theory is appropriate. Therefore, although we see a list of various theories, which may be bewildering, it does not lead to the suffering of "not knowing what to do." Moreover, the judgments made on each theory in the book allow us to generate the effect of mutual learning and discussion based on different viewpoints and research.

These are all the strengths of this book. It is published by Shanghai Hanwen Zhengkai Printing Bureau and is priced at one yuan.

At the same time, we also have an incidental feeling, which is that the value of this book is relatively long-lasting. Although administrative laws and regulations are constantly being revised, added to, and deleted, the sources of administrative law are nothing more than orders, regulations, and other items. Therefore, to study administrative law, it is necessary to continuously collect information on administration for reference and to make research practically suitable. This book can serve as basic reading material. Complete

"How to Study Philosophy" 198

— Yan Yilin

Written by Wang Te-fu, published by Jiang Bookstore

(I)

Recently, several introductory books on philosophy have been published. In my opinion, only two are worth noting. One is Ai Siqi's "Popular Philosophy," which is a popular philosophy book in a conversational style, suitable for the general public to read—as its name suggests. The other is Wang Te-fu's "How to Study Philosophy," which will be discussed here. This is a very excellent philosophy book; although it is presented as an "introductory book," it is actually more than just an excellent introductory book. People who have never known the content of the discipline of "philosophy" can not only clearly understand what problems "philosophy" contains or how these problems are related by reading this book, but it can even tell you where these problems lead to. This is something that people who have confusedly read hundreds of philosophy books may not be able to answer.

This book is divided into nine chapters, each divided into three or two sections. Chapter 1, "What is the Nature of Philosophy?", Chapter 2, "Why Should We Study Philosophy?", and Chapter 3, "The Positive and Empirical Methods in Philosophical Research" are the first part of the book and can be regarded as a general overview. Chapter 4, "How to Conduct Analytical Research", Chapter 5, "How to Conduct Synthetic Research", Chapter 6, "How to Conduct Critical Research", and Chapter 7, "The Steps to Take in Research" are the second part of the book and can be regarded as the "main discussion." Chapter 8, "Outline of Philosophy (I) - An Overview of the Contents of Philosophy," and Chapter 9, "Outline of Philosophy (II) - An Overview of the History of the Development of Philosophy" provide a cross-sectional and longitudinal explanation of philosophy. The above is the outline of the whole book. The author will not hesitate to be tedious, select and restate its internal content, and then discuss its main characteristics and value.

(II)

It is necessary to make a brief summary of the content of the whole book, whether in introducing a book or criticizing a book. What follows is the main content of the entire book "How to Study Philosophy." As for the method of summary, it is to extract the key points by chapter and state the central meaning of each chapter.

1. What is Philosophy: Philosophy is a department of science and is qualified to be called science, because what is called science is the objective things and the laws of their movement, which are reflected and transformed into a systematically organized system of knowledge of human thinking; and philosophy as a discipline is to systematize the general and fundamental principles of nature, society and its relationship with human thinking, making it a comprehensive, organized and systematic knowledge. In other words, it is the same in using these laws to restate the relationship between objective existence, thinking, and existence, thereby discussing the most general and most fundamental laws of all existence, forming its own knowledge system and becoming a regular discipline; from this, it can be seen that philosophy is indeed a rigorous science. Specifically speaking, when the overall universe is the subject of research, it is the object dealt with by natural philosophy or cosmology philosophy; when the overall society is the subject of research, it is the object dealt with by social philosophy; when human thinking and its relationship with general existence are the subject matter, it is the object dealt with by the pure thinking philosophy's theory of knowledge and methodology. This is also the type of philosophy that is distinguished by the realistic object of research. In short, when philosophy discusses existence, thinking, and even their interrelationships, it comprehensively studies the most general and fundamental laws of motion in the universe, the highest peak of science, which is the science of condensed matter of the entire theory of scientific theory and method. From a methodological point of view, it can be said to be the "algebra of science."

2. Why Study Philosophy: The study of philosophy is necessary both to understand the universe, society, and life, and to practice. Our study of philosophy lies in being able to form a system of thought of a worldview, a social view, and a view of life for ourselves, and to obtain the correct worldview, social view, and view of life to guide our actions. Demand is caused by the actual life of mankind, and in order to continue living, we must have a correct philosophical system of thought as a guide for progress—everything new is to be. Creation guided by a correct worldview and outlook on life.

Principal Changes Profession to Postman 209

— Wu Ci

It is said that a school principal is a "lucrative position," especially in public schools. However, this "lucrative position" now seems not even as good as "chicken ribs," because although chicken ribs are tasteless to eat, it is still a pity to discard them. Wenling Correspondence: Wang Yungao, principal of Guanxiao Cai Elementary School (formerly the Fifth County Elementary School) in the western district of this county... Now, because the cost of living is increasing, and a monthly income of a dozen yuan is not enough to make ends meet, he took the postman exam at the Wenling Post Office the other day. Yesterday, I heard that Mr. Wang has already submitted his resignation from the position of principal to the county government..."

The principal here should actually be called an elementary school principal. To put it more precisely, it should be an inland elementary school principal. Because many university presidents drive cars and live in Western-style houses. Even some principals of public and private primary and secondary schools are well-fed and clothed. In Borneo 212

— Li Liwen

—Encounter One—

The boat entered the mouth of Santiaou Bay, and the seawater gradually became lighter.

The night breeze gently blew up. The setting sun reflected a vast and brilliant scene on the sea. Fishermen returning from the sea were rowing their small boats——the night breeze lightly carried the gentle sound of the oars that often evoke infinite thoughts in people——slightly——creak——creak——

Page 20

People were crowding on one side of the deck, and a complex emotion was gently scratching at their hearts. On the shore, the gray-blue, mighty mountains, the verdant trees, and the exquisite wooden houses painted in various colors, seemed to be sleeping in the golden afterglow of the setting sun, silently and colorlessly radiating a premonition of tranquility and happiness.

The stern rumbled——rumbled——splashed——churning up a pile of turbid yellow waves, and the boat stopped trembling.

I got off the boat, carrying my only luggage——a half-new imitation leather suitcase, and walked for several hours on the narrow, dark streets of Santiaou, then, stuffed a few pieces of "Roti" (Note 1) into my pocket, and got on that yellow, old, long-distance bus.

In the car, I swallowed two pieces of Roti——and fell into a daze and fell asleep. Several days of life at sea had not allowed me to be quiet, and fatigue seemed to erupt at me all at once. A Dutch ticket inspector woke me up, and I subconsciously handed over my ticket, and then fell back into a dazed sleep. When a kind fellow passenger woke me up, I had already——arrived in Bangka.

I rubbed my sleepy eyes, and in the sky, golden brilliance had already shone, shining on my back with a slight warmth. Several Bornean natives (Note 2) with strange clothes and fierce looks passed by me, and a peculiar smell almost made me sneeze.

I walked along a small road onto the bustling Dabogong Street. At the end of the street, I found the place that made me cross mountains and rivers with my only hope——a not-so-large grocery store. I excitedly and hesitantly stepped inside. My sister's husband was busy copying something at the counter, and the shop assistants cast strange glances at me. I walked to the front of the counter——my brother-in-law looked up, and I seemed to see something from his long-unseen, round, plump, ruddy face, and almost wanted to jump in and hug him——and go wild with joy... However, my brother-in-law's cold, almost expressionless gaze stopped me, and he simply uttered a sentence to me:

"You're here?"

I didn't answer, something deeply stimulated me, making my whole body tremble slightly: I wanted to hold my brother-in-law's hand and ask him why he had hurt my feelings like this——but I didn't do it, but instead humbly and almost pleadingly narrated everything that had happened, I told him how I had begged acquaintances for travel expenses and came to Borneo with such a passionate heart...

"Brother-in-law," I said——a tear suddenly rolled down my nose. "Give me a job, any kind of job——I can take care of myself."

"Young man——everything has changed now. I am really saddened by the degeneration of young people. Actually, why is it necessary to do this? Everyone has their own duty!"

"This is not our problem, brother-in-law, please give me a job! I promise you, I am a very good worker——don't think I ran away from school."

My brother-in-law yawned at length. "You are an excessively stubborn person. Look here——there won't be a job that suits you!"

"No——no," I almost shouted out. "As long as it is a job, it doesn't matter where you send me——I am suitable for anything."

My brother-in-law fell silent, shaking his head slightly like a pendulum, and picked up the pen with one hand——and began to write.

When closing the shop in the evening, my brother-in-law handed over five shields, giving me a deadly blow like an arrow with that cold, expressionless tone:

"You should go back on the boat you came on. You don't need to go to your sister's grave——the bus leaves at 8:10, go early and you might be able to get a good seat."

I stood blankly under the dim kerosene lamp, I wanted to cry, and I wanted to laugh heartily——suddenly I snatched the money from my brother-in-law's hand, picked up the suitcase——and rushed out. ...

On the street, a night atmosphere was looming, and the mighty mountains of Borneo were dimly overlooking everything with their towering shadows. The shops had closed their wooden doors, and a faint yellow light leaked from the gaps in the boards.

I strode forward, one hand still tightly grasping that paper shield, and a slight coolness of the Borneo sea breeze was felt on my body.

Note 1: Roti, Malay: bread.

Note 2: There are two kinds of Borneo savages——one lives in the deep mountains all year round, eating raw meat and drinking blood, and the other lives scattered in the foothills, communicating with people. The former is called: raw savage, the latter is called: cooked savage.

Impressions After Seeing the First National Cartoon Exhibition 213

— Xu Ji

("In the decline of a chaotic age, writing emerges"—Xunzi)

In fact, it is not necessarily writing; all art, all art produced in the hands of artists living in a chaotic world, inevitably presents a kind of helpless smiling tears. However, this "helplessness" does not mean that people are truly helpless. On the contrary, it shows that the artists of a generation have worked hard to actively find solutions in helplessness.

This characteristic exists not only in all outstanding essays in modern times, but also in the emerging folk art of cartoons.

People are becoming smarter. Nowadays, no writer, whether writing or painting, circles around certain prescribed themes. Expanding the scope of creative themes is a gratifying phenomenon. Because, as Mr. Lu Xun said, we not only remember "we," but we must also remember "they" outside of us: similarly, we not only have to describe "great work," but also describe "debauchery and shamelessness."

This has been quite well expressed in the three emerging arts of essays, prints, and cartoons in recent years. Although there may still be room for further discussion technically, the suffering of people in chaotic times, the ardent longing for light, the hatred of the baseness of the world... etc. can be seen.—Even if the art of a chaotic age is inevitably put on a different face, this face still makes us feel more noble and lovable than the face of a dog.

These emotions were quite evident in all the more than two hundred works in the First National Cartoon Exhibition. Because we still remember the various practical difficulties, in this regard, even if we sometimes feel that it is somewhat "poor," we no longer make excessive complaints.

The name "cartoon" at this exhibition is quite broad. It not only refers to the general so-called "caricature" (Cariture) (naturally, this is the most in number), but also includes "sketches," book illustrations (such as Cao Hanmei's "Golden Lotus" meticulous brushwork), and even "poster designs" (National Cartoon Exhibition posters). And the content, like the form, is very multifaceted. The lack of a central temperament seems to be a regret that cannot be ignored. In terms of highly accomplished techniques, we must mention Cao Hanmei's "Golden Lotus illustrations" and Zhang Guangyu's "Hanging Branches". In addition, Ye Qianyu's "Portrait of a Certain Lady," Zimei's "Anna May Wong," and Zhang Wenyuan's "Grand View Garden" also gave us very hard-to-remove good impressions. However, it seems that the most thrilling ones are not these delicate and exquisite works. Three works that used great intelligence in terms of technique and gave people clear and understandable themes should be cited: "The Country is Broken, the Mountains and Rivers Remain" (Gao Longsheng), "Tai Chi Diagram" (Shao Yucun), and "Only the State Magistrate is Allowed to Set Fires" (Lin Daoan). That kind of expression method that makes people know at a glance should be one of the main characteristics of cartoons. I personally do not admire those obscure things that are not easy to understand. Of course, this is due to the poverty of personal artistic cultivation, but I think that if cartoons really should belong to the masses, then those grotesque and mysterious brushstrokes are not a good path. Modern artists have gotten rid of a strange concept and no longer regard making their works incomprehensible as a proud goal.

This decision to hold an exhibition had a lot of visitors. People hope to find their own pain, tears, cries, and comfort in the hard work of the artists. I don't think this is an excessive request, right? And in this regard, when we recall the past print exhibitions, we cannot help but feel a little demanding in terms of content achievement.

However, even so, we saw the hard work of the organizers and creators—in front of the torn map, what more can we ask for?

A Certain School Seeks an Elementary School Teacher 214

— Ding Li Zuo
